      <p><b>El Salvador</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ɔːr/: 'ar' in 'war'">ɔːr</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-El_Salvador.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/En-us-El_Salvador.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-El Salvador.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>; <small>Spanish:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[el salβaˈðoɾ]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:ES-pe_-_El_Salvador.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e5/ES-pe_-_El_Salvador.ogg" class="internal" title="ES-pe - El Salvador.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>, literally "<a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">The Saviour</a>"), officially the <b>Republic of El Salvador</b> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es">República de El Salvador</i>), is a country in <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>. It is bordered on the northeast by <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a>, on the northwest by <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a>, and on the south by the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>. El Salvador's capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/San_Salvador" title="San Salvador">San Salvador</a>. As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the country had a population of approximately 6.42 million.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-5">[5]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>For millennia, the region was controlled by several <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerican</a> nations, especially <a href="/wiki/Lenca" title="Lenca">Lenca</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-:1_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-10">[10]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maya_peoples" title="Maya peoples">Mayans</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> then later the <a href="/wiki/Kuskatan/Cuzcatan_(Cuzcatlan)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kuskatan/Cuzcatan (Cuzcatlan)">Cuzcatlecs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Archaeological monuments also suggest an early <a href="/wiki/Olmecs" title="Olmecs">Olmec</a> presence around the first millennium BC.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> In the beginning of the 16th century, the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_El_Salvador" title="Spanish conquest of El Salvador">Spanish Empire conquered</a> the Central American territory, incorporating it into the Viceroyalty of <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a> ruled from <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>. However the Viceroyalty of Mexico had little to no influence in the daily affairs of the isthmus, which was colonized in 1524. In 1609, the area was declared the <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Guatemala" title="Captaincy General of Guatemala">Captaincy General of Guatemala</a> by the Spanish, which included the territory that would become El Salvador until its independence from Spain in 1821. It was forcefully incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/First_Mexican_Empire" title="First Mexican Empire">First Mexican Empire</a>, then later seceded, joining the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Central_America" title="Federal Republic of Central America">Federal Republic of Central America</a> in 1823. When the republic dissolved in 1841, El Salvador became a sovereign nation, then formed a short-lived union with Honduras and <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a> called the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Republic_of_Central_America" title="Greater Republic of Central America">Greater Republic of Central America</a>, which lasted from 1895 to 1898.<sup id="cite_ref-Boland2001_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boland2001-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IhrieOropesa2011_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IhrieOropesa2011-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Haskin2012_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haskin2012-16">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>From the late 19th to the mid-20th century, El Salvador endured chronic political and economic instability characterized by coups, revolts, and a succession of authoritarian rulers. Persistent socioeconomic inequality and civil unrest culminated in the devastating <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_Civil_War" title="Salvadoran Civil War">Salvadoran Civil War</a> from 1979 to 1992, fought between the military-led government backed by the United States, and a coalition of left-wing <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla</a> groups. The conflict ended with the <a href="/wiki/Chapultepec_Peace_Accords" title="Chapultepec Peace Accords">Chapultepec Peace Accords</a>. This negotiated settlement established a multiparty constitutional republic, which remains in place to this day. </p>
      <p>While this Civil War was going on in the country large numbers of Salvadorans emigrated to the United States, and by 2008 they were one of the largest immigrant groups in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>El Salvador's economy has historically been dominated by agriculture, beginning with the Spanish taking control of the indigenous cacao crop in the 16th century, with production centered in <a href="/wiki/Izalco" title="Izalco">Izalco</a>, and the use of balsam from the ranges of <a href="/wiki/La_Libertad_Department_(El_Salvador)" title="La Libertad Department (El Salvador)">La Libertad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ahuachap%C3%A1n_Department" title="Ahuachapán Department">Ahuachapan</a>. This was followed by a boom in use of the <a href="/wiki/Indigofera" title="Indigofera">indigo plant</a> (<i>añil</i> in Spanish) in the 19th century, mainly for its use as a dye.<sup id="cite_ref-Montgomery1995_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Montgomery1995-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Murray1997_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murray1997-19">[19]</a></sup> Thereafter the focus shifted to <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a>, which by the early 20th century accounted for 90% of export earnings.<sup id="cite_ref-Boland2001b_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boland2001b-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pearcy2006_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pearcy2006-21">[21]</a></sup> El Salvador has since reduced its dependence on coffee and embarked on diversifying its economy by opening up trade and financial links and expanding the manufacturing sector.<sup id="cite_ref-FoleyHapipi2005_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FoleyHapipi2005-22">[22]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_col%C3%B3n" title="Salvadoran colón">colón</a>, the currency of El Salvador since 1892, was replaced by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">United States dollar</a> in 2001, by Francisco Flores.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>El Salvador ranks 14th among Latin American countries in terms of the Human Development Index and fourth in Central America (behind <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> partly because of ongoing rapid industrialization.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> However, the country continues to struggle with high rates of poverty, inequality, and gang-related violent crime. </p>

          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Religion"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Religion</span></a></li> 
         </ul> </li> 
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Conquistador <a href="/wiki/Pedro_de_Alvarado" title="Pedro de Alvarado">Pedro de Alvarado</a> named the new province after <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a> Christ – San Salvador (lit. "Saint Savior"). The territory's name, including the province of <a href="/wiki/San_Miguel,_El_Salvador" title="San Miguel, El Salvador">San Miguel</a>, was later extended to the <i><i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">Provincia De Nuestro Señor Jesus Cristo, El Salvador Del Mundo</i></i> (<abbr title="literal translation">lit.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap"> </span>'Province of our Lord Jesus Christ, the Saviour of the World'), shortened to the Republic of El Salvador, or Salvador, during the post-Federal Republic period and subsequently settled on as <i><i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">El Salvador</i></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_El_Salvador" title="History of El Salvador">History of El Salvador</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistoric">Prehistoric</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistoric">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Toma2.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Toma2.gif/220px-Toma2.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Toma2.gif/330px-Toma2.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Toma2.gif/440px-Toma2.gif 2x" data-file-width="623" data-file-height="541"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Toma2.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Excavation of a <a href="/wiki/Megatherium" title="Megatherium">Megatherium</a> in the Tomayate site <a href="/wiki/Apopa" title="Apopa">Apopa</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Toma4.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Toma4.gif/220px-Toma4.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Toma4.gif/330px-Toma4.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Toma4.gif/440px-Toma4.gif 2x" data-file-width="596" data-file-height="418"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Toma4.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Skull fossil of an ancient horse in the Tomayate site <a href="/wiki/Apopa" title="Apopa">Apopa</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Tomayate is a palaeontological site located on the banks of the river of the same name in the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Apopa" title="Apopa">Apopa</a>. The site has produced abundant Salvadoran <a href="/wiki/Megafauna" title="Megafauna">megafauna</a> fossils belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a>. The palaeontological site was discovered accidentally in 2000, and in the following year, an excavation by the Museum of Natural History of El Salvador revealed several remnants of <a href="/wiki/Cuvieronius" title="Cuvieronius">Cuvieronius</a> and 18 other species of vertebrates including <a href="/wiki/Giant_tortoise" title="Giant tortoise">giant tortoises</a>, <a href="/wiki/Megatherium" title="Megatherium">Megatherium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glyptodon" title="Glyptodon">Glyptodon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toxodon" title="Toxodon">Toxodon</a>, extinct horses, paleo-llamas. The site stands out from most Central American Pleistocene deposits, being more ancient and much richer, which provides valuable information of the <a href="/wiki/Great_American_Interchange" title="Great American Interchange">Great American Interchange</a>, in which the Central American isthmus land bridge was paramount. At the same time, it is considered the richest vertebrate site in Central America and one of the largest accumulations of <a href="/wiki/Proboscidea" title="Proboscidea">proboscideans</a> in the Americas. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian">Pre-Columbian</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Pre-Columbian">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Temazcal_en_Joya_de_Cer%C3%A9n.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Temazcal_en_Joya_de_Cer%C3%A9n.jpg/220px-Temazcal_en_Joya_de_Cer%C3%A9n.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Temazcal_en_Joya_de_Cer%C3%A9n.jpg/330px-Temazcal_en_Joya_de_Cer%C3%A9n.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Temazcal_en_Joya_de_Cer%C3%A9n.jpg/440px-Temazcal_en_Joya_de_Cer%C3%A9n.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Temazcal_en_Joya_de_Cer%C3%A9n.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Temazcal in Joya de Ceren.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Sophisticated civilization in El Salvador dates to its settlement by the indigenous <a href="/wiki/Lenca" title="Lenca">Lenca</a> people; theirs was the first and the oldest indigenous civilization to settle in there.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-10">[10]</a></sup> They were a union of Central American tribes that oversaw most of the isthmus from southern Guatemala to northern Panama, which they called Managuara.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The Lenca of eastern El Salvador trace their origins to specific caves with ancient pictographs dating back to at least 600 AD<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> and some sources say as far back as 7000 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> There was also a presence of Olmecs, although their role is unclear. Their influence remains recorded in the form of stone monuments and artefacts preserved in western El Salvador, as well as the national museum.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> A Mayan population settled there in the <a href="/wiki/Formative_stage" title="Formative stage">Formative</a> period, but their numbers were greatly diminished when the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ilopango" title="Lake Ilopango">Ilopango</a> supervolcano eruption caused a massive exodus.<sup id="cite_ref-Campbell1985_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campbell1985-29">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Centuries later the area's occupants were displaced by the <a href="/wiki/Pipil_people" title="Pipil people">Pipil people</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nahuan_languages" title="Nahuan languages">Nahua</a> speaking groups who migrated from <a href="/wiki/Anahuac_(Aztec)" title="Anahuac (Aztec)">Anahuac</a> beginning around 800 AD and occupied the central and western regions of El Salvador.<sup id="cite_ref-Campbell1985_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campbell1985-29">[29]</a></sup> The Nahua Pipil were the last indigenous people to arrive in El Salvador.<sup id="cite_ref-Fowler1991_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fowler1991-30">[30]</a></sup> They called their territory <i>Kuskatan</i>, a <a href="/wiki/Nawat_language" title="Nawat language">Nawat</a> word<sup id="cite_ref-Cárdenas1950_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cárdenas1950-31">[31]</a></sup> meaning "The Place of Precious Jewels," <a href="/wiki/Back-formation" title="Back-formation">back-formed</a> into <a href="/wiki/Classical_Nahuatl" title="Classical Nahuatl">Classical Nahuatl</a> <i>Cōzcatlān</i>, and Hispanicized as <i>Cuzcatlán</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Baratta1951_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baratta1951-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cárdenas1964_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cárdenas1964-33">[33]</a></sup> It was the largest domain in Salvadoran territory up until European contact. The term <i>Cuzcatleco</i> is commonly used to identify someone of Salvadoran heritage, although the majority of the eastern population has indigenous heritage of Lenca origin, as do their place names such as <a href="/wiki/Intipuc%C3%A1" title="Intipucá">Intipuca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chirilagua" title="Chirilagua">Chirilagua</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lolotique" title="Lolotique">Lolotique</a>. </p>
      <p>Most of the archaeological sites in western El Salvador such as <a href="/wiki/Lake_G%C3%BCija" title="Lake Güija">Lago de Guija</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joya_de_Cer%C3%A9n" title="Joya de Cerén">Joya De Ceren</a> indicate a pre-Columbian Mayan culture. <a href="/wiki/Cihuat%C3%A1n" title="Cihuatán">Cihuatan</a> shows signs of material trade with northern Nahua culture, eastern Mayan and Lenca culture, and southern Nicaraguan and Costa Rican indigenous culture.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tazumal" title="Tazumal">Tazumal</a>'s smaller B1-2 structure shows a <a href="/wiki/Talud-tablero" title="Talud-tablero">talud</a>-<a href="/wiki/Talud-tablero" title="Talud-tablero">tablero</a> style of architecture that is associated with Nahua culture and corresponds with their migration history from Anahuac. In eastern El Salvador, the Lenca site of <a href="/wiki/Quelepa" title="Quelepa">Quelepa</a> is highlighted as a major pre-Columbian cultural center and demonstrates links to the Mayan site of <a href="/wiki/Cop%C3%A1n" title="Copán">Copan</a> in western Honduras as well as the previously mentioned sites in <a href="/wiki/Chalchuapa" title="Chalchuapa">Chalchuapa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cara_Sucia_(Mesoamerican_site)" title="Cara Sucia (Mesoamerican site)">Cara Sucia</a> in western El Salvador. An investigation of the site of La Laguna in <a href="/wiki/Usulut%C3%A1n" title="Usulután">Usulutan</a> has also produced Copador items which link it to the Lenca-Maya trade route. </p> 
      <h3><span id="European_arrival_.281522.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="European_arrival_(1522)">European arrival (1522)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: European arrival (1522)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>By 1521, the indigenous population of the Mesoamerican area had been drastically reduced by the <a href="/wiki/History_of_smallpox" title="History of smallpox">smallpox epidemic</a> that was spreading throughout the territory, although it had not yet reached pandemic levels in Cuzcatlán or the northern portion Managuara.<sup id="cite_ref-Peters2005_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peters2005-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Card2007_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Card2007-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The first known visit by Spaniards to what is now Salvadoran territory was made by the admiral <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Ni%C3%B1o" title="Andrés Niño">Andrés Niño</a>, who led an expedition to Central America. He disembarked in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Fonseca" title="Gulf of Fonseca">Gulf of Fonseca</a> on 31 May 1522, at <a href="/wiki/Meanguera_del_Golfo" title="Meanguera del Golfo">Meanguera island</a>, naming it Petronila,<sup id="cite_ref-Valdés2006_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Valdés2006-38">[38]</a></sup> and then traversed to <a href="/wiki/Jiquilisco_Bay" title="Jiquilisco Bay">Jiquilisco Bay</a> on the mouth of <a href="/wiki/Lempa_River" title="Lempa River">Lempa River</a>. The first indigenous people to have contact with the Spanish were the Lenca of eastern El Salvador. </p> 
      <h4><span id="Conquest_of_Cuzcatl.C3.A1n_and_Managuara"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Conquest_of_Cuzcatlán_and_Managuara">Conquest of Cuzcatlán and Managuara</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Conquest of Cuzcatlán and Managuara">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_El_Salvador" title="Spanish conquest of El Salvador">Spanish conquest of El Salvador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pedro_de_Alvarado.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Pedro_de_Alvarado.JPG/170px-Pedro_de_Alvarado.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="234" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Pedro_de_Alvarado.JPG/255px-Pedro_de_Alvarado.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Pedro_de_Alvarado.JPG/340px-Pedro_de_Alvarado.JPG 2x" data-file-width="580" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pedro_de_Alvarado.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Spanish Conquistador <a href="/wiki/Pedro_de_Alvarado" title="Pedro de Alvarado">Pedro de Alvarado</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1524, after participating in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Aztec_Empire" title="Spanish conquest of the Aztec Empire">conquest of the Aztec Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_de_Alvarado" title="Pedro de Alvarado">Pedro de Alvarado</a>, his brother Gonzalo, and their men crossed the <a href="/wiki/Paz_River" title="Paz River">Rio Paz</a> southward into Cuzcatlec territory. The Spaniards were disappointed to discover that the Pipil had no gold or jewels like those they had found in Guatemala or Mexico,<sup id="cite_ref-Minahan2013_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minahan2013-39">[39]</a></sup> but they recognized the richness of the land's volcanic soil. </p>
      <p>Pedro Alvarado led the first incursion to extend their dominion to the domain of Cuzcatlan in June 1524.<sup id="cite_ref-NicholsPool2012_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NicholsPool2012-40">[40]</a></sup> When he arrived at the borders of the kingdom, he saw that civilians had been evacuated. Cuzcatlec warriors moved to the coastal city of <a href="/wiki/Acajutla" title="Acajutla">Acajutla</a> and waited for Alvarado and his forces. Alvarado approached, confident that the result would be similar to what occurred in Mexico and Guatemala. He thought he would easily deal this new indigenous force since the Mexican allies on his side and the Pipil spoke a similar language.<sup id="cite_ref-Pan_AmericanUnion1934_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pan_AmericanUnion1934-41">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Alvarado described the Cuzcatlec soldiers as having shields decorated with colourful exotic feathers, a vest-like armour made of three inch cotton which arrows could not penetrate, and long spears. Both armies suffered many casualties, with a wounded Alvarado retreating and losing a lot of his men, especially among the Mexican Indian auxiliaries. Once his army had regrouped, Alvarado decided to head to the Cuzcatlan capital and again faced armed Cuzcatlec. Wounded, unable to fight and hiding in the cliffs, Alvarado sent his Spanish men on their horses to approach the Cuzcatlec to see if they would fear the horses, but they did not retreat, Alvarado recalls in his letters to <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Cort%C3%A9s" title="Hernán Cortés">Hernán Cortés</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Cuzcatlec attacked again, and on this occasion stole Spanish weaponry. Alvarado retreated and sent Mexican messengers to demand that the Cuzcatlec warriors return the stolen weapons and surrender to their opponent's king. The Cuzcatlec responded with the famous response, "If you want your weapons, come get them". As days passed, Alvarado, fearing an ambush, sent more Mexican messengers to negotiate, but these messengers never came back and were presumably executed. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tazumal_10.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Tazumal_10.jpg/220px-Tazumal_10.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Tazumal_10.jpg/330px-Tazumal_10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Tazumal_10.jpg/440px-Tazumal_10.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1386"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tazumal_10.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Tazumal" title="Tazumal">Tazumal</a> ruins in Santa Ana, El Salvador.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Spanish efforts were firmly resisted by Pipil and their Mayan-speaking neighbours. They defeated the Spaniards and what was left of their <a href="/wiki/Tlaxcala" title="Tlaxcala">Tlaxcalan</a> allies, forcing them to withdraw to Guatemala. After being wounded, Alvarado abandoned the war and appointed his brother, <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_de_Alvarado" title="Gonzalo de Alvarado">Gonzalo de Alvarado</a>, to continue the task. Two subsequent expeditions (the first in 1525, followed by a smaller group in 1528) brought the Pipil under Spanish control, since the Pipil also were weakened by a regional epidemic of smallpox. In 1525, the conquest of Cuzcatlán was completed and the city of San Salvador was established. The Spanish faced much resistance from the Pipil and were not able to reach eastern El Salvador, the area of the Lencas. </p>
      <p>In 1526 the Spanish founded the garrison town of <a href="/wiki/San_Miguel,_El_Salvador" title="San Miguel, El Salvador">San Miguel</a> in northern Managuara—territory of the Lenca, headed by another explorer and conquistador, <a href="/wiki/Luis_de_Moscoso_Alvarado" title="Luis de Moscoso Alvarado">Luis de Moscoso Alvarado</a>, nephew of Pedro Alvarado. Oral history holds that a Maya-Lenca crown princess, Antu Silan Ulap I, organized resistance to the conquistadors.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The kingdom of the Lenca was alarmed by de Moscoso's invasion, and Antu Silan travelled from village to village, uniting all the Lenca towns in present-day El Salvador and Honduras against the Spaniards. Through surprise attacks and overwhelming numbers, they were able to drive the Spanish out of San Miguel and destroy the garrison. </p>
      <p>For ten years the Lencas prevented the Spanish from building a permanent settlement. Then the Spanish returned with more soldiers, including about 2,000 forced conscripts from indigenous communities in Guatemala. They pursued the Lenca leaders further up into the mountains of <a href="/wiki/Intibuc%C3%A1_Department" title="Intibucá Department">Intibucá</a>. </p>
      <p>Antu Silan Ulap eventually handed over control of the Lenca resistance to <a href="/wiki/Lempira_(Lenca_ruler)" title="Lempira (Lenca ruler)">Lempira</a> (also called Empira). Lempira was noteworthy among indigenous leaders in that he mocked the Spanish by wearing their clothes after capturing them and using their weapons captured in battle. Lempira fought in command of thousands of Lenca forces for six more years in Managuara until he was killed in battle. The remaining Lenca forces retreated into the hills. The Spanish were then able to rebuild their garrison town of San Miguel in 1537. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Colonial_period_.281525.E2.80.931821.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_period_(1525–1821)">Colonial period (1525–1821)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Colonial period (1525–1821)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Proclama_de_libertad_(indep._Centroam%C3%A9rica).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Proclama_de_libertad_%28indep._Centroam%C3%A9rica%29.jpg/220px-Proclama_de_libertad_%28indep._Centroam%C3%A9rica%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Proclama_de_libertad_%28indep._Centroam%C3%A9rica%29.jpg/330px-Proclama_de_libertad_%28indep._Centroam%C3%A9rica%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Proclama_de_libertad_%28indep._Centroam%C3%A9rica%29.jpg/440px-Proclama_de_libertad_%28indep._Centroam%C3%A9rica%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1166" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Proclama_de_libertad_(indep._Centroam%C3%A9rica).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A painting of the First Independence Movement celebration in San Salvador. At the centre, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mat%C3%ADas_Delgado" title="José Matías Delgado">José Matías Delgado</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Manuel_Jos%C3%A9_Arce_y_Fagoaga.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Manuel_Jos%C3%A9_Arce_y_Fagoaga.jpg/170px-Manuel_Jos%C3%A9_Arce_y_Fagoaga.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Manuel_Jos%C3%A9_Arce_y_Fagoaga.jpg/255px-Manuel_Jos%C3%A9_Arce_y_Fagoaga.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Manuel_Jos%C3%A9_Arce_y_Fagoaga.jpg/340px-Manuel_Jos%C3%A9_Arce_y_Fagoaga.jpg 2x" data-file-width="767" data-file-height="990"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Manuel_Jos%C3%A9_Arce_y_Fagoaga.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Manuel_Jos%C3%A9_Arce" title="Manuel José Arce">Manuel José Arce</a> joined the movement for independence from Spain, joining in the first Cry for Independence on 5 November 1811 in San Salvador.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the colonial period, San Salvador and San Miguel were part of the Captaincy General of Guatemala, also known as the Kingdom of Guatemala (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es">Reino de Guatemala</i>), created in 1609 as an administrative division of <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a>. The Salvadoran territory was administered by the Mayor of Sonsonate, with San Salvador being established as an <i><a href="/wiki/Intendancy_of_San_Salvador" title="Intendancy of San Salvador">intendencia</a></i> in 1786. </p>
      <p>In 1811, a combination of internal and external factors motivated Central American elites to attempt to gain independence from the Spanish Crown. The most important internal factors were the desire of local elites to control the country's affairs free of involvement from Spanish authorities, and the long-standing Creole aspiration for independence. The main external factors motivating the independence movement were the success of the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American</a> revolutions in the 18th century, and the weakening of the Spanish Crown's military power as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, with the resulting inability to control its colonies effectively. </p>
      <p>In November 1811 Salvadoran priest <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mat%C3%ADas_Delgado" title="José Matías Delgado">José Matías Delgado</a> rang the bells of Iglesia La Merced in San Salvador, calling for insurrection and launching the <a href="/wiki/1811_Independence_Movement" title="1811 Independence Movement">1811 Independence Movement</a>. This insurrection was suppressed, and many of its leaders were arrested and served sentences in jail. Another insurrection was launched in 1814, which was also suppressed. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Independence_.281821.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(1821)">Independence (1821)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Independence (1821)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Firma_del_Acta_de_Independencia_de_Centroam%C3%A9rica.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Firma_del_Acta_de_Independencia_de_Centroam%C3%A9rica.jpg/350px-Firma_del_Acta_de_Independencia_de_Centroam%C3%A9rica.jpg" decoding="async" width="350" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Firma_del_Acta_de_Independencia_de_Centroam%C3%A9rica.jpg/525px-Firma_del_Acta_de_Independencia_de_Centroam%C3%A9rica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Firma_del_Acta_de_Independencia_de_Centroam%C3%A9rica.jpg/700px-Firma_del_Acta_de_Independencia_de_Centroam%C3%A9rica.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1544" data-file-height="686"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Firma_del_Acta_de_Independencia_de_Centroam%C3%A9rica.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A painting by <a href="/wiki/Chilean_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Chilean people">Chilean</a> painter <a href="/w/index.php?title=Luis_Vergara_Ahumada&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Luis Vergara Ahumada (page does not exist)">Luis Vergara Ahumada</a>, depicting the signing of the Act by Father <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mat%C3%ADas_Delgado" title="José Matías Delgado">José Matías Delgado</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p> In 1821 in light of unrest in Guatemala, Spanish authorities capitulated and signed the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Independence_of_Central_America" title="Act of Independence of Central America">Act of Independence of Central America</a>, which released all of the Captaincy of Guatemala (comprising current territories of Guatemala, El Salvador, Honduras, Nicaragua and Costa Rica and the Mexican state of <a href="/wiki/Chiapas" title="Chiapas">Chiapas</a>) from Spanish rule and declared its independence. In 1821, El Salvador joined Costa Rica, Guatemala, Honduras and Nicaragua in a union named the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Central_America" title="Federal Republic of Central America">Federal Republic of Central America</a>. </p>
      <p>In early 1822, the authorities of the newly independent Central American provinces, meeting in Guatemala City, voted to join the newly constituted <a href="/wiki/First_Mexican_Empire" title="First Mexican Empire">First Mexican Empire</a> under <a href="/wiki/Agust%C3%ADn_de_Iturbide" title="Agustín de Iturbide">Agustín de Iturbide</a>. El Salvador resisted, insisting on autonomy for the Central American countries. A Mexican military detachment marched to San Salvador and suppressed dissent, but with the fall of Iturbide on 19 March 1823, the army decamped back to Mexico. Shortly thereafter, the authorities of the provinces revoked the vote to join Mexico, deciding instead to form a federal union of the five remaining provinces. (Chiapas permanently joined Mexico at this juncture.) When the Federal Republic of Central America dissolved in 1841, El Salvador maintained its own government until it joined Honduras and Nicaragua in 1896 to form the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Republic_of_Central_America" title="Greater Republic of Central America">Greater Republic of Central America</a>, which dissolved in 1898. </p>
      <p>After the mid-19th century, the economy was based on coffee growing. As the world market for indigo withered away, the economy prospered or suffered as the world coffee price fluctuated. The enormous profits that coffee yielded as a monoculture export served as an impetus for the concentration of land into the hands of an oligarchy of just a few families.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Throughout the last half of the 19th century, a succession of presidents from the ranks of the Salvadoran oligarchy, nominally both conservative and liberal, generally agreed on the promotion of coffee as the predominant <a href="/wiki/Cash_crop" title="Cash crop">cash crop</a>, the development of infrastructure (railroads and port facilities) primarily in support of the coffee trade, the elimination of communal landholdings to facilitate further coffee production, the passage of anti-<a href="/wiki/Vagrancy" title="Vagrancy">vagrancy</a> laws to ensure that displaced <a href="/wiki/Peasant" title="Peasant">campesinos</a> and other rural residents provided sufficient labour for the coffee fincas (plantations), and the suppression of rural discontent. In 1912, the national guard was created as a rural police force. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tomas_Regalado1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Tomas_Regalado1.jpg/170px-Tomas_Regalado1.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="251" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Tomas_Regalado1.jpg/255px-Tomas_Regalado1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Tomas_Regalado1.jpg/340px-Tomas_Regalado1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2292" data-file-height="3389"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tomas_Regalado1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Gen. Tomás Regalado
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1898, General <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_Regalado_(Salvadoran_politician)" title="Tomás Regalado (Salvadoran politician)">Tomas Regalado</a> gained power by force, deposing <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Antonio_Guti%C3%A9rrez" title="Rafael Antonio Gutiérrez">Rafael Antonio Gutiérrez</a> and ruling as president until 1903. Once in office he revived the practice of presidents designating their successors. After serving his term, he remained active in the Army of El Salvador and was killed 11 July 1906, at El Jicaro during a <a href="/wiki/Totoposte_Wars" title="Totoposte Wars">war against Guatemala</a>. Until 1913 El Salvador was politically stable, with undercurrents of popular discontent. When President <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Enrique_Araujo" title="Manuel Enrique Araujo">Manuel Enrique Araujo</a> was killed in 1913, many hypotheses were advanced for the political motive of his murder. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Civil_Ensign_of_El_Salvador.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Civil_Ensign_of_El_Salvador.svg/170px-Civil_Ensign_of_El_Salvador.svg.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="102" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Civil_Ensign_of_El_Salvador.svg/255px-Civil_Ensign_of_El_Salvador.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Civil_Ensign_of_El_Salvador.svg/340px-Civil_Ensign_of_El_Salvador.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Civil_Ensign_of_El_Salvador.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Dios, Union, Libertad (God, Union, Liberty) El Salvador 1912 Flag.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Araujo's administration was followed by the Melendez-Quinonez dynasty that lasted from 1913 to 1927. <a href="/wiki/P%C3%ADo_Romero_Bosque" title="Pío Romero Bosque">Pio Romero Bosque</a>, ex-Minister of the Government and a trusted collaborator of the dynasty, succeeded President <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Mel%C3%A9ndez" title="Jorge Meléndez">Jorge Meléndez</a> and in 1930 announced free elections, in which <a href="/wiki/Arturo_Araujo" title="Arturo Araujo">Arturo Araujo</a> came to power on 1 March 1931 in what was considered the country's first freely contested election. His government lasted only nine months before it was overthrown by junior military officers who accused his Labor Party of lacking political and governmental experience and of using its government offices inefficiently. President Araujo faced general popular discontent, as the people had expected economic reforms and the redistribution of land. There were demonstrations in front of the National Palace from the first week of his administration. His vice president and minister of war was General <a href="/wiki/Maximiliano_Hern%C3%A1ndez_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="Maximiliano Hernández Martínez">Maximiliano Hernández Martínez</a>. </p>
      <p>In December 1931, a <a href="/wiki/1931_Salvadoran_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1931 Salvadoran coup d'état">coup d'état was organized</a> by junior officers and led by Martínez. Only the First Regiment of Cavalry and the National Police defended the presidency (the National Police had been on its payroll), but later that night, after hours of fighting, the badly outnumbered defenders surrendered to rebel forces. The Directorate, composed of officers, hid behind a shadowy figure,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> a rich anti-Communist banker called Rodolfo Duke, and later installed the ardent fascist Martínez as president. The revolt was probably caused by the army's discontent at not having been paid by President Araujo for some months. Araujo left the National Palace and unsuccessfully tried to organize forces to defeat the revolt. </p>
      <p>The U.S. Minister in El Salvador met with the Directorate and later recognized the government of Martínez, which agreed to hold presidential elections. He resigned six months prior to running for re-election, winning back the presidency as the only candidate on the ballot. He ruled from 1935 to 1939, then from 1939 to 1943. He began a fourth term in 1944 but resigned in May after a general strike. Martínez had said he was going to respect the constitution, which stipulated he could not be re-elected, but he refused to keep his promise. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="La_Matanza">La Matanza</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: La Matanza">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>From December 1931, the year of the coup that brought Martínez to power, there was brutal suppression of rural resistance. The most notable event was the February <a href="/wiki/La_Matanza" title="La Matanza">1932 Salvadoran peasant uprising</a>, originally led by <a href="/wiki/Farabundo_Mart%C3%AD" title="Farabundo Martí">Farabundo Martí</a> and Abel Cuenca, and university students Alfonso Luna and Mario Zapata, but these leaders were captured before the planned insurrection. Only Cuenca survived; the other insurgents were killed by the government. After the capture of the movement leaders, the insurrection erupted in a disorganized and mob-controlled fashion, resulting in government repression that was later referred to as La Matanza (The Massacre), because tens of thousands of citizens died in the ensuing chaos on the orders of President Martinez. </p>
      <p>In the unstable political climate of the previous few years, the social activist and revolutionary leader Farabundo Martí helped found the Communist Party of Central America, and led a Communist alternative to the Red Cross called International Red Aid, serving as one of its representatives. Their goal was to help poor and underprivileged Salvadorans through the use of <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="Marxism–Leninism">Marxist-Leninist</a> ideology (strongly rejecting <a href="/wiki/Stalinism" title="Stalinism">Stalinism</a>). In December 1930, at the height of the country's economic and social depression, Martí was once again exiled because of his popularity among the nation's poor and rumours of his upcoming nomination for president the following year. Once Arturo Araujo was elected president in 1931, Martí returned to El Salvador, and along with Alfonso Luna and Mario Zapata began the movement that was later truncated by the military. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Jos%C3%A9_Napole%C3%B3n_Duarte_1987b.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Jos%C3%A9_Napole%C3%B3n_Duarte_1987b.jpg/170px-Jos%C3%A9_Napole%C3%B3n_Duarte_1987b.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Jos%C3%A9_Napole%C3%B3n_Duarte_1987b.jpg/255px-Jos%C3%A9_Napole%C3%B3n_Duarte_1987b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Jos%C3%A9_Napole%C3%B3n_Duarte_1987b.jpg/340px-Jos%C3%A9_Napole%C3%B3n_Duarte_1987b.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3332" data-file-height="2265"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Jos%C3%A9_Napole%C3%B3n_Duarte_1987b.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Napole%C3%B3n_Duarte" title="José Napoleón Duarte">José Napoleón Duarte</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>They helped start a guerrilla revolt of indigenous farmers. The government responded by killing over 30,000 people at what was to have been a "peaceful meeting" in 1932. The peasant uprising against Martínez was crushed by the Salvadoran military ten days after it had begun. The Communist-led rebellion, fomented by collapsing coffee prices, enjoyed some initial success, but was soon drowned in a bloodbath. President Martínez, who had toppled an elected government only weeks earlier, ordered the defeated Martí shot after a perfunctory hearing. </p>
      <p>Historically, the high Salvadoran population density has contributed to tensions with neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a>, as land-poor Salvadorans emigrated to less densely populated Honduras and established themselves as squatters on unused or underused land. This phenomenon was a major cause of the <a href="/wiki/Football_War" title="Football War">1969 Football War</a> between the two countries.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> As many as 130,000 Salvadorans were forcibly expelled or fled from Honduras.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Party_(El_Salvador)" title="Christian Democratic Party (El Salvador)">Christian Democratic Party</a> (PDC) and the <a href="/wiki/National_Coalition_Party_(El_Salvador)" title="National Coalition Party (El Salvador)">National Conciliation Party</a> (PCN) were active in Salvadoran politics from 1960 until 2011, when they were disbanded by the Supreme Court because they had failed to win enough votes in the 2004 presidential election;<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Both parties have since reconstituted. They share common ideals, but one represents the middle class and the latter the interests of the Salvadoran military. </p>
      <p>PDC leader <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Napole%C3%B3n_Duarte" title="José Napoleón Duarte">José Napoleón Duarte</a> was the mayor of <a href="/wiki/San_Salvador" title="San Salvador">San Salvador</a> from 1964 to 1970, winning three elections during the regime of PCN President <a href="/wiki/Julio_Adalberto_Rivera_Carballo" title="Julio Adalberto Rivera Carballo">Julio Adalberto Rivera Carballo</a>, who allowed free elections for mayors and the National Assembly. Duarte later ran for president with a political grouping called the <a href="/wiki/National_Opposition_Union" title="National Opposition Union">National Opposition Union</a> (UNO) but was defeated in the 1972 presidential elections. He lost to the ex-Minister of Interior, Col. <a href="/wiki/Arturo_Armando_Molina" title="Arturo Armando Molina">Arturo Armando Molina</a>, in an election that was widely viewed as fraudulent; Molina was declared the winner even though Duarte was said to have received a majority of the votes. Duarte, at some army officers' request, supported a revolt to protest the election fraud, but was captured, tortured and later exiled. Duarte returned to the country in 1979 to enter politics after working on projects in Venezuela as an engineer. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Salvadoran_Civil_War_.281979.E2.80.931992.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Salvadoran_Civil_War_(1979–1992)">Salvadoran Civil War (1979–1992)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Salvadoran Civil War (1979–1992)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_Civil_War" title="Salvadoran Civil War">Salvadoran Civil War</a>
      </div> 
      <p>On 15 October 1979, a <a href="/wiki/1979_Salvadoran_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1979 Salvadoran coup d'état">coup d'état</a> brought the <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Government_Junta_of_El_Salvador" title="Revolutionary Government Junta of El Salvador">Revolutionary Government Junta of El Salvador</a> to power. It nationalized many private companies and took over much privately owned land. The purpose of this new junta was to stop the revolutionary movement already underway in response to Duarte's stolen election. Nevertheless, the oligarchy opposed <a href="/wiki/Agrarian_reform" title="Agrarian reform">agrarian reform</a>, and a junta formed with young liberal elements from the army such as <a href="/wiki/Adolfo_Arnoldo_Majano" title="Adolfo Arnoldo Majano">Gen. Majano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jaime_Abdul_Guti%C3%A9rrez" title="Jaime Abdul Gutiérrez">Gen. Gutierrez</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> as well as with progressives such as <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_Ungo" title="Guillermo Ungo">Guillermo Ungo</a> and Alvarez. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Masakro-%C4%89e-Suchitoto-Salvadoro.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Masakro-%C4%89e-Suchitoto-Salvadoro.jpg/220px-Masakro-%C4%89e-Suchitoto-Salvadoro.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Masakro-%C4%89e-Suchitoto-Salvadoro.jpg/330px-Masakro-%C4%89e-Suchitoto-Salvadoro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Masakro-%C4%89e-Suchitoto-Salvadoro.jpg/440px-Masakro-%C4%89e-Suchitoto-Salvadoro.jpg 2x" data-file-width="818" data-file-height="546"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Masakro-%C4%89e-Suchitoto-Salvadoro.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A billboard serving as a reminder of one of many <a href="/wiki/List_of_massacres_in_El_Salvador" title="List of massacres in El Salvador">massacres</a> that occurred during the civil war.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Pressure from the oligarchy soon dissolved the junta because of its inability to control the army in its repression of the people fighting for unionization rights, agrarian reform, better wages, accessible health care and freedom of expression. In the meantime, the guerrilla movement was spreading to all sectors of Salvadoran society. Middle and high school students were organized in MERS (Movimiento Estudiantil Revolucionario de Secundaria, Revolutionary Movement of Secondary Students); college students were involved with AGEUS (Asociacion de Estudiantes Universitarios Salvadorenos; Association of Salvadoran College Students); and workers were organized in BPR (Bloque Popular Revolucionario, Popular Revolutionary Block). In October 1980, several other major guerrilla groups of the Salvadoran left had formed the <a href="/wiki/Farabundo_Mart%C3%AD_National_Liberation_Front" title="Farabundo Martí National Liberation Front">Farabundo Martí National Liberation Front</a>, or FMLN. By the end of the 1970s, government-contracted death squads were killing about 10 people each day. Meanwhile, the FMLN had 6,000 – 8,000 active guerrillas and hundreds of thousands of part-time militia, supporters, and sympathizers.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ERP_combatants_Perqu%C3%ADn_1990_24.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/ERP_combatants_Perqu%C3%ADn_1990_24.jpg/220px-ERP_combatants_Perqu%C3%ADn_1990_24.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/ERP_combatants_Perqu%C3%ADn_1990_24.jpg/330px-ERP_combatants_Perqu%C3%ADn_1990_24.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/ERP_combatants_Perqu%C3%ADn_1990_24.jpg/440px-ERP_combatants_Perqu%C3%ADn_1990_24.jpg 2x" data-file-width="736" data-file-height="500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ERP_combatants_Perqu%C3%ADn_1990_24.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Farabundo_Mart%C3%AD_National_Liberation_Front" title="Farabundo Martí National Liberation Front">ERP</a> combatants in <a href="/wiki/Perqu%C3%ADn" title="Perquín">Perquín</a>, 1990.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The U.S. supported and financed the creation of a second junta to change the political environment and stop the spread of a leftist insurrection. Napoleón Duarte was recalled from his exile in Venezuela to head this new junta. However, a revolution was already underway and his new role as head of the junta was seen by the general population as opportunistic. He was unable to influence the outcome of the insurrection. <a href="/wiki/%C3%93scar_Romero" title="Óscar Romero">Óscar Romero</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> Archbishop of San Salvador, denounced injustices and massacres committed against civilians by government forces. He was considered "the voice of the voiceless", but he was assassinated by a <a href="/wiki/Death_squad" title="Death squad">death squad</a> while saying Mass on 24 March 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Some consider this to be the beginning of the full <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_Civil_War" title="Salvadoran Civil War">Salvadoran Civil War</a>, which lasted from 1980 to 1992. An unknown number of people "disappeared" during the conflict, and the UN reports that more than 75,000 were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_Army" title="Salvadoran Army">Salvadoran Army</a>'s US-trained <a href="/wiki/Atlacatl_Battalion" title="Atlacatl Battalion">Atlacatl Battalion</a> was responsible for the <a href="/wiki/El_Mozote_massacre" title="El Mozote massacre">El Mozote massacre</a> where more than 800 civilians were murdered, over half of them children, the <a href="/wiki/El_Calabozo_massacre" title="El Calabozo massacre">El Calabozo massacre</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Murder_of_UCA_scholars" class="mw-redirect" title="Murder of UCA scholars">murder of UCA scholars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Radio_Venceremos_Reconstruction.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Radio_Venceremos_Reconstruction.jpg/220px-Radio_Venceremos_Reconstruction.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Radio_Venceremos_Reconstruction.jpg/330px-Radio_Venceremos_Reconstruction.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Radio_Venceremos_Reconstruction.jpg/440px-Radio_Venceremos_Reconstruction.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Radio_Venceremos_Reconstruction.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A reconstruction of <a href="/wiki/Radio_Venceremos" title="Radio Venceremos">Radio Venceremos</a>, at the <a href="/wiki/Museo_de_la_Palabra_y_la_Imagen" title="Museo de la Palabra y la Imagen">Museo de la Palabra y la Imagen</a>, San Salvador.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 16 January 1992, the government of El Salvador, represented by president <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Cristiani" title="Alfredo Cristiani">Alfredo Cristiani</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/FMLN" class="mw-redirect" title="FMLN">FMLN</a>, represented by the commanders of the five guerrilla groups – <a href="/wiki/Shafik_Handal" class="mw-redirect" title="Shafik Handal">Shafik Handal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joaqu%C3%ADn_Villalobos" title="Joaquín Villalobos">Joaquín Villalobos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salvador_S%C3%A1nchez_Cer%C3%A9n" title="Salvador Sánchez Cerén">Salvador Sánchez Cerén</a>, Francisco Jovel and <a href="/wiki/Ferm%C3%A1n_Cienfuegos" title="Fermán Cienfuegos">Eduardo Sancho</a>, all signed peace agreements brokered by the United Nations ending the 12-year civil war. This event, held at <a href="/wiki/Chapultepec_Castle" title="Chapultepec Castle">Chapultepec Castle</a> in Mexico, was attended by U.N. dignitaries and other representatives of the international community. After signing the armistice, the president stood up and shook hands with all the now ex-guerrilla commanders, an action which was widely admired. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Post-war_.281992.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_(1992–present)">Post-war (1992–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Post-war (1992–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The so-called <a href="/wiki/Chapultepec_Peace_Accords" title="Chapultepec Peace Accords">Chapultepec Peace Accords</a> mandated reductions in the size of the army, and the dissolution of the National Police, the Treasury Police, the National Guard and the Civilian Defence, a paramilitary group. A new Civil Police was to be organized. Judicial immunity for crimes committed by the armed forces ended; the government agreed to submit to the recommendations of a <a href="/wiki/Commission_on_the_Truth_for_El_Salvador" class="mw-redirect" title="Commission on the Truth for El Salvador">Commission on the Truth for El Salvador</a> <i>(Comisión de la Verdad Para El Salvador)</i>, which would "investigate serious acts of violence occurring since 1980, and the nature and effects of the violence, and...recommend methods of promoting national reconciliation". In 1993 the Commission delivered its findings reporting human rights violations on both sides of the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Five days later the El Salvadoran legislature passed an amnesty law for all acts of violence during the period. </p>
      <p>From 1989 until 2004, Salvadorans favoured the <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Republican_Alliance" title="Nationalist Republican Alliance">Nationalist Republican Alliance</a> (ARENA) party, voting in ARENA presidents in every election (<a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Cristiani" title="Alfredo Cristiani">Alfredo Cristiani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armando_Calder%C3%B3n_Sol" title="Armando Calderón Sol">Armando Calderón Sol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Flores_P%C3%A9rez" title="Francisco Flores Pérez">Francisco Flores Pérez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Saca" title="Antonio Saca">Antonio Saca</a>) until 2009. The unsuccessful attempts of the left-wing party to win presidential elections led to its selection of a journalist rather than a former guerrilla leader as a candidate. On 15 March 2009, <a href="/wiki/Mauricio_Funes" title="Mauricio Funes">Mauricio Funes</a>, a television figure, became the first president from the <a href="/wiki/Farabundo_Mart%C3%AD_National_Liberation_Front" title="Farabundo Martí National Liberation Front">Farabundo Martí National Liberation Front</a> (FMLN) party. He was inaugurated on 1 June 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> One focus of the Funes government has been revealing the alleged corruption from the past government.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>ARENA formally expelled Saca from the party in December 2009. With 12 loyalists in the National Assembly, Saca established his own party, GANA (Gran Alianza por la Unidad Nacional or <a href="/wiki/Grand_Alliance_for_National_Unity" title="Grand Alliance for National Unity">Grand Alliance for National Unity</a>), and entered into a tactical legislative alliance with the FMLN.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> After three years in office, with Saca's GANA party providing the FMLN with a legislative majority, Funes had not taken action to either investigate or to bring corrupt former officials to justice. </p>
      <p>Economic reforms since the early 1990s brought major benefits in terms of improved social conditions, diversification of the export sector, and access to international financial markets at investment grade level. Crime remains a major problem for the investment climate. Early in the new millennium, El Salvador's government created the Ministerio de Medio Ambiente y Recursos Naturales&nbsp;— the Ministry of Environment and Natural Resources (MARN)&nbsp;— in response to climate change concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-cdkn.org_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cdkn.org-59">[59]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In March 2014, <a href="/wiki/Salvador_Sanchez_Ceren" class="mw-redirect" title="Salvador Sanchez Ceren">Salvador Sanchez Ceren</a> of the FMLN narrowly won the <a href="/wiki/2014_Salvadoran_presidential_election" title="2014 Salvadoran presidential election">election</a>. He sworn in as president on 31 May 2014. He was the first former guerrilla to become the President of El Salvador.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcnews_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcnews-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In October 2017, an El Salvador court ruled that former leftist President Mauricio Funes, in office since 2009 until 2014, and one of his sons, had illegally enriched themselves. Funes had sought asylum in Nicaragua in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>in September 2018, former conservative President Antonio “Tony” Saca, in office since 2004 until 2009, was sentenced to 10 years in prison after he pleaded guilty to diverting more than US$300 million in state funds to his own businesses and third parties.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 1 June 2019, <a href="/wiki/Nayib_Bukele" title="Nayib Bukele">Nayib Bukele</a> became the new President of El Salvador.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Bukele was the winner of February <a href="/wiki/2019_Salvadoran_presidential_election" title="2019 Salvadoran presidential election">2019 presidential election</a>. He represented the GANA (National Alliance), an ultraconservative party. Two main parties, left-wing FMLN and the conservative Arena, had dominated politics in El Salvador over the past three decades.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to a report by the International Crisis Group (ICG) 2020, the homicide rates, murders in El Salvador had dropped by as much as 60 percent since Bukele became president in June 2019. The reason might have been a “non-aggression deal” between parts of the government and the gangs.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bukele was exceptionally popular among the citizens. According to a survey, 96 percent of respondents said he was doing a “good” or “very good job. El Salvador's <a href="/wiki/2021_Salvadoran_legislative_election" title="2021 Salvadoran legislative election">legislative elections</a> were an important breakthrough in February 2021. The new party, <a href="/wiki/Nuevas_Ideas" title="Nuevas Ideas">Nuevas Ideas</a>, or New Ideas, founded by Bukele, won around two-thirds of the vote with its allies (GANA-New Ideas). His party won supermajority of 56 seats in the 84-seat parliament. The supermajority enables Bukele to appoint judges and to pass laws, for instance, to remove presidential term limits.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-centralamerica_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-centralamerica-67">[67]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_El_Salvador" title="Geography of El Salvador">Geography of El Salvador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:612px;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Cerro_verde.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Cerro_verde.jpg/610px-Cerro_verde.jpg" decoding="async" width="610" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Cerro_verde.jpg/915px-Cerro_verde.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Cerro_verde.jpg/1220px-Cerro_verde.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="450"></a> 
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Cerro_verde.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
          </div>Panoramic of <a href="/wiki/Coatepeque_Caldera" title="Coatepeque Caldera">Coatepeque Caldera</a>, Cerro Verde and <a href="/wiki/Izalco_(volcano)" title="Izalco (volcano)">Izalco (volcano)</a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Un-el-salvador.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Un-el-salvador.png/290px-Un-el-salvador.png" decoding="async" width="290" height="216" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Un-el-salvador.png/435px-Un-el-salvador.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Un-el-salvador.png/580px-Un-el-salvador.png 2x" data-file-width="2590" data-file-height="1926"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Un-el-salvador.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of El Salvador
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:El_Salvador_Topography.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/El_Salvador_Topography.png/260px-El_Salvador_Topography.png" decoding="async" width="260" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/El_Salvador_Topography.png/390px-El_Salvador_Topography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/El_Salvador_Topography.png/520px-El_Salvador_Topography.png 2x" data-file-width="1963" data-file-height="1797"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:El_Salvador_Topography.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>El Salvador's topography.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>El Salvador lies in the isthmus of Central America between latitudes <a href="/wiki/13th_parallel_north" title="13th parallel north">13°</a> and <a href="/wiki/15th_parallel_north" title="15th parallel north">15°N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/87th_meridian_west" title="87th meridian west">87°</a> and <a href="/wiki/91st_meridian_west" title="91st meridian west">91°W</a>. It stretches 270&nbsp;km (168&nbsp;mi) from west-northwest to east-southeast and 142&nbsp;km (88&nbsp;mi) north to south, with a total area of 21,041&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (8,124&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). As the smallest country in continental America, El Salvador is affectionately called <i>Pulgarcito de America</i> (the "<a href="/wiki/Tom_Thumb" title="Tom Thumb">Tom Thumb</a> of the Americas"). El Salvador shares borders with Guatemala and Honduras, the total national boundary length is 546&nbsp;km (339&nbsp;mi): 126 miles (203&nbsp;km) with Guatemala and 343&nbsp;km (213&nbsp;mi) with Honduras. It is the only Central American country that has no Caribbean coastline. The coastline on the Pacific is 307&nbsp;km (191&nbsp;mi) long. </p>
      <p>El Salvador has over 300 rivers, the most important of which is the <a href="/wiki/Lempa_River" title="Lempa River">Rio Lempa</a>. Originating in Guatemala, the Rio Lempa cuts across the northern range of mountains, flows along much of the central plateau, and cuts through the southern volcanic range to empty into the Pacific. It is El Salvador's only navigable river. It and its tributaries drain about half of the country's area. Other rivers are generally short and drain the Pacific lowlands or flow from the central plateau through gaps in the southern mountain range to the Pacific. These include the <a href="/wiki/Goascor%C3%A1n_River" title="Goascorán River">Goascorán</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jiboa_River" title="Jiboa River">Jiboa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Torola_River" title="Torola River">Torola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paz_River" title="Paz River">Paz</a> and the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande_de_San_Miguel" title="Río Grande de San Miguel">Río Grande de San Miguel</a>. </p>
      <p>There are several lakes enclosed by volcanic craters in El Salvador, the most important of which are <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ilopango" title="Lake Ilopango">Lake Ilopango</a> (70&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> or 27&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Coatepeque" class="mw-redirect" title="Lake Coatepeque">Lake Coatepeque</a> (26&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> or 10&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). <a href="/wiki/Lake_G%C3%BCija" title="Lake Güija">Lake Güija</a> is El Salvador's largest natural lake (44&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> or 17&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). Several artificial lakes were created by the damming of the Lempa, the largest of which is <a href="/wiki/Cerr%C3%B3n_Grande_Reservoir" title="Cerrón Grande Reservoir">Cerrón Grande Reservoir</a> (135&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> or 52&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). There are a total 320&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (123.6&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) of water within El Salvador's borders. </p>
      <p>The highest point in El Salvador is <a href="/wiki/Cerro_El_Pital" title="Cerro El Pital">Cerro El Pital</a>, at 2,730 metres (8,957&nbsp;ft), on the border with Honduras. Two parallel mountain ranges cross El Salvador to the west with a central plateau between them and a narrow coastal plain hugging the Pacific. These physical features divide the country into two physiographic regions. The mountain ranges and central plateau, covering 85% of the land, comprise the interior highlands. The remaining coastal plains are referred to as the Pacific lowlands. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_El_Salvador" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of El Salvador">Climate of El Salvador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
