        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_SLV_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Koppen-Geiger_Map_SLV_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_SLV_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="104" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Koppen-Geiger_Map_SLV_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_SLV_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Koppen-Geiger_Map_SLV_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_SLV_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1794" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_SLV_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Köppen climate classification of El Salvador.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>El Salvador has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a> with pronounced wet and dry seasons. Temperatures vary primarily with elevation and show little seasonal change. The Pacific lowlands are uniformly hot; the central plateau and mountain areas are more moderate. The rainy season extends from May to October; this time of year is referred to as <i>invierno</i> or winter. Almost all the annual rainfall occurs during this period; yearly totals, particularly on southern-facing mountain slopes, can be as high as 2170&nbsp;mm. Protected areas and the central plateau receive less, although still significant, amounts. Rainfall during this season generally comes from low pressure systems formed over the Pacific and usually falls in heavy afternoon thunderstorms. </p>
      <p>From November through April, the northeast <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">trade winds</a> control weather patterns; this time of year is referred to as <i>verano</i>, or summer. During these months, air flowing from the Caribbean has lost most of its precipitation while passing over the mountains in Honduras. By the time this air reaches El Salvador, it is dry, hot, and hazy, and the country experiences hot weather, excluding the northern higher mountain ranges, where temperatures are generally cooler. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_disasters">Natural disasters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Natural disasters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Extreme_weather_events">Extreme weather events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Extreme weather events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Salcoatit%C3%A1n,_El_Salvador_-_panoramio_(9).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Salcoatit%C3%A1n%2C_El_Salvador_-_panoramio_%289%29.jpg/220px-Salcoatit%C3%A1n%2C_El_Salvador_-_panoramio_%289%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Salcoatit%C3%A1n%2C_El_Salvador_-_panoramio_%289%29.jpg/330px-Salcoatit%C3%A1n%2C_El_Salvador_-_panoramio_%289%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Salcoatit%C3%A1n%2C_El_Salvador_-_panoramio_%289%29.jpg/440px-Salcoatit%C3%A1n%2C_El_Salvador_-_panoramio_%289%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Salcoatit%C3%A1n,_El_Salvador_-_panoramio_(9).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Volcanic range, <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_de_Apaneca" title="Cordillera de Apaneca">Cordillera de Apaneca</a>, view from <a href="/wiki/Salcoatit%C3%A1n" title="Salcoatitán">Salcoatitán</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>El Salvador's position on the Pacific Ocean also makes it subject to severe weather conditions, including heavy rainstorms and severe droughts, both of which may be made more extreme by the <a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o" title="El Niño">El Niño</a> and <a href="/wiki/La_Ni%C3%B1a" title="La Niña">La Niña</a> effects.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Hurricanes occasionally form in the Pacific with the notable exception of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Mitch" title="Hurricane Mitch">Hurricane Mitch</a>, which formed in the Atlantic and crossed Central America. </p>
      <p>In the summer of 2001 a severe drought destroyed 80% of El Salvador's crops, causing famine in the countryside.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> On 4 October 2005, severe rains resulted in dangerous flooding and landslides, which caused at least 50 deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-tdfiyp_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tdfiyp-71">[71]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Earthquakes_and_volcanic_activity">Earthquakes and volcanic activity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Earthquakes and volcanic activity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vulkan_Chaparrastique,_El_Salvador_2013_01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Vulkan_Chaparrastique%2C_El_Salvador_2013_01.JPG/220px-Vulkan_Chaparrastique%2C_El_Salvador_2013_01.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Vulkan_Chaparrastique%2C_El_Salvador_2013_01.JPG/330px-Vulkan_Chaparrastique%2C_El_Salvador_2013_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Vulkan_Chaparrastique%2C_El_Salvador_2013_01.JPG/440px-Vulkan_Chaparrastique%2C_El_Salvador_2013_01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vulkan_Chaparrastique,_El_Salvador_2013_01.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/San_Miguel_(volcano)" title="San Miguel (volcano)">San Miguel</a> volcano in 2013
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>El Salvador lies along the Pacific <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_Fire" title="Ring of Fire">Ring of Fire</a> and is thus subject to significant tectonic activity, including frequent <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">earthquakes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanic</a> activity. The capital San Salvador was destroyed in 1756 and 1854, and it suffered heavy damage in the 1919, 1982, and 1986 tremors. Recent examples include the earthquake on 13 January 2001 that measured 7.7 on the <a href="/wiki/Richter_magnitude_scale" title="Richter magnitude scale">Richter magnitude scale</a> and caused a <a href="/wiki/Landslide" title="Landslide">landslide</a> that killed more than 800 people;<sup id="cite_ref-tdfiyp_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tdfiyp-71">[71]</a></sup> and another earthquake only a month later, on 13 February 2001, that killed 255 people and damaged about 20% of the nation's housing. A <a href="/wiki/Moment_magnitude_scale" title="Moment magnitude scale">5.7 M<sub>w</sub></a> earthquake in 1986 resulted in 1,500 deaths, 10,000 injuries, and 100,000 people left homeless.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>El Salvador has over twenty volcanoes; two of them, San Miguel and <a href="/wiki/Izalco_(volcano)" title="Izalco (volcano)">Izalco</a>, have been active in recent years. From the early 19th century to the mid-1950s, Izalco erupted with a regularity that earned it the name "Lighthouse of the Pacific". Its brilliant flares were clearly visible for great distances at sea, and at night its glowing lava turned it into a brilliant luminous cone. The most recent destructive volcanic eruption took place on 1 October 2005, when the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Volcano" title="Santa Ana Volcano">Santa Ana Volcano</a> spewed a cloud of ash, hot mud and rocks that fell on nearby villages and caused two deaths. The most severe volcanic eruption in this area occurred in the 5th century AD when the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ilopango" title="Lake Ilopango">Ilopango</a> volcano erupted with a <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_Explosivity_Index" title="Volcanic Explosivity Index">VEI</a> strength of 6, producing widespread <a href="/wiki/Pyroclastic_flow" title="Pyroclastic flow">pyroclastic flows</a> and devastating <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Mayan cities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eumomota_superciliosa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Eumomota_superciliosa.jpg/220px-Eumomota_superciliosa.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Eumomota_superciliosa.jpg/330px-Eumomota_superciliosa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Eumomota_superciliosa.jpg/440px-Eumomota_superciliosa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="741" data-file-height="613"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eumomota_superciliosa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Torogoz" class="mw-redirect" title="Torogoz">torogoz</a> is El Salvador's national bird.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>It is estimated that there are 500 species of birds, 1,000 species of butterflies, 400 species of orchids, 800 species of trees, and 800 species of marine fish in El Salvador. </p>
      <p>There are eight species of sea turtles in the world; six of them nest on the coasts of Central America, and four make their home on the Salvadoran coast: the <a href="/wiki/Leatherback_sea_turtle" title="Leatherback sea turtle">leatherback turtle</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hawksbill_sea_turtle" title="Hawksbill sea turtle">hawksbill</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Green_sea_turtle" title="Green sea turtle">green sea turtle</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Olive_ridley_sea_turtle" title="Olive ridley sea turtle">olive ridley</a>. The hawksbill is critically endangered. </p>
      <p>Recent conservation efforts provide hope for the future of the country's biological diversity. In 1997, the government established the Ministry of the Environment and Natural Resources. A general environmental framework law was approved by the National Assembly in 1999. Several non-governmental organizations are doing work to safeguard some of the country's most important forested areas. Foremost among these is SalvaNatura, which manages El Impossible, the country's largest national park under an agreement with El Salvador's environmental authorities. </p>
      <p>El Salvador is home to six terrestrial ecosystems: <a href="/wiki/Central_American_montane_forests" title="Central American montane forests">Central American montane forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre_de_Chiapas_moist_forests" title="Sierra Madre de Chiapas moist forests">Sierra Madre de Chiapas moist forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_American_dry_forests" title="Central American dry forests">Central American dry forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_American_pine-oak_forests" class="mw-redirect" title="Central American pine-oak forests">Central American pine-oak forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Fonseca_mangroves" title="Gulf of Fonseca mangroves">Gulf of Fonseca mangroves</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Dry_Pacific_Coast_mangroves" title="Northern Dry Pacific Coast mangroves">Northern Dry Pacific Coast mangroves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-75">[75]</a></sup> It had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 4.05/10, ranking it 136th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-76">[76]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The 1983 constitution has the highest legal authority in the country. El Salvador has a democratic and representative government, whose three bodies are: </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sesion_Solemne_de_Legislatura_2015-2018_(17866066655).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Sesion_Solemne_de_Legislatura_2015-2018_%2817866066655%29.jpg/220px-Sesion_Solemne_de_Legislatura_2015-2018_%2817866066655%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Sesion_Solemne_de_Legislatura_2015-2018_%2817866066655%29.jpg/330px-Sesion_Solemne_de_Legislatura_2015-2018_%2817866066655%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Sesion_Solemne_de_Legislatura_2015-2018_%2817866066655%29.jpg/440px-Sesion_Solemne_de_Legislatura_2015-2018_%2817866066655%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sesion_Solemne_de_Legislatura_2015-2018_(17866066655).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Salvadoran cadets in the Legislative Assembly of El Salvador
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <ol>
       <li>The Executive Branch, headed by the President of the Republic, who is elected by direct vote and remains in office for five years with no re-election but he can be elected after sitting out one electoral period. The president has a Cabinet of Ministers whom he appoints, and is also the Commander-in-Chief of the Armed Forces.</li> 
       <li>The Legislative Branch, called El Salvador's Legislative Assembly (unicameral), consisting of 84 deputies.</li> 
       <li>The Judiciary, headed by the Supreme Court, which is composed of 15 judges, one of them being elected as President of the Judiciary.</li>
      </ol> 
      <p>The political framework of El Salvador is a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a> with a multiform, multi-party system. The <a href="/wiki/President_of_El_Salvador" title="President of El Salvador">President</a>, currently <a href="/wiki/Nayib_Bukele" title="Nayib Bukele">Nayib Bukele</a>, is both <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government. <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">Legislative power</a> is vested in both the government and the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_El_Salvador" title="Legislative Assembly of El Salvador">Legislative Assembly</a>. The country also has an independent judiciary and <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_El_Salvador" title="Supreme Court of El Salvador">Supreme Court</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_El_Salvador" title="Politics of El Salvador">Politics of El Salvador</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_El_Salvador" title="List of political parties in El Salvador">List of political parties in El Salvador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ANIVERSARIO_DE_LA_CONSTITUCION_(23168818313).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/ANIVERSARIO_DE_LA_CONSTITUCION_%2823168818313%29.jpg/220px-ANIVERSARIO_DE_LA_CONSTITUCION_%2823168818313%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/ANIVERSARIO_DE_LA_CONSTITUCION_%2823168818313%29.jpg/330px-ANIVERSARIO_DE_LA_CONSTITUCION_%2823168818313%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/ANIVERSARIO_DE_LA_CONSTITUCION_%2823168818313%29.jpg/440px-ANIVERSARIO_DE_LA_CONSTITUCION_%2823168818313%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ANIVERSARIO_DE_LA_CONSTITUCION_(23168818313).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_El_Salvador" title="Legislative Assembly of El Salvador">Legislative Assembly of El Salvador</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>El Salvador has a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>. Two <a href="/wiki/Political_parties" class="mw-redirect" title="Political parties">political parties</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Republican_Alliance" title="Nationalist Republican Alliance">Nationalist Republican Alliance</a> (ARENA) and the <a href="/wiki/Farabundo_Mart%C3%AD_National_Liberation_Front" title="Farabundo Martí National Liberation Front">Farabundo Martí National Liberation Front</a> (FMLN) have tended to dominate elections. ARENA candidates won four consecutive presidential elections until the election of <a href="/wiki/Mauricio_Funes" title="Mauricio Funes">Mauricio Funes</a> of the FMLN in March 2009. The FMLN Party is leftist in ideology, and is split between the dominant <a href="/wiki/Marxist-Leninist" class="mw-redirect" title="Marxist-Leninist">Marxist-Leninist</a> faction in the legislature, and the <a href="/wiki/Social_liberalism" title="Social liberalism">social liberal</a> wing led by President Funes. However, the two-party dominance was broken after <a href="/wiki/Nayib_Bukele" title="Nayib Bukele">Nayib Bukele</a>,a candidate from <a href="/wiki/Grand_Alliance_for_National_Unity" title="Grand Alliance for National Unity">GANA</a> won the <a href="/wiki/2019_Salvadoran_presidential_election" title="2019 Salvadoran presidential election">2019 Salvadoran presidential election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Geographically, <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_El_Salvador" title="Departments of El Salvador">the departments</a> of the Central region, especially the capital and the coastal regions, known as departamentos rojos, or red departments, are relatively Leftist. The departamentos azules, or blue departments in the east, western and highland regions are relatively conservative. The winner of the <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_presidential_election,_2014" class="mw-redirect" title="Salvadoran presidential election, 2014">2014 presidential election</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salvador_S%C3%A1nchez_Cer%C3%A9n" title="Salvador Sánchez Cerén">Salvador Sánchez Cerén</a> belongs to the FMLN party.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcnews_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcnews-60">[60]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2015_Salvadoran_legislative_election" title="2015 Salvadoran legislative election">2015 elections</a> for mayors and members of the National Assembly, ARENA appeared to be the winner with tight control of the National Assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In February 2021, the results of <a href="/wiki/2021_Salvadoran_legislative_election" title="2021 Salvadoran legislative election">legislative election</a> caused a major change in the politics of El Salvador. The new party of popular president Nayib Bukele, <a href="/wiki/Nuevas_Ideas" title="Nuevas Ideas">Nuevas Ideas</a> (New Ideas) with its allies won the biggest congressional majority in the country's history.<sup id="cite_ref-centralamerica_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-centralamerica-67">[67]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations_and_military">Foreign relations and military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Foreign relations and military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_El_Salvador" title="Foreign relations of El Salvador">Foreign relations of El Salvador</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_El_Salvador" title="Armed Forces of El Salvador">Armed Forces of El Salvador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_Participates_in_Signing_Ceremony_for_the_CSL_Lease_Extension_-_48342132177.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Secretary_Pompeo_Participates_in_Signing_Ceremony_for_the_CSL_Lease_Extension_-_48342132177.jpg/220px-Secretary_Pompeo_Participates_in_Signing_Ceremony_for_the_CSL_Lease_Extension_-_48342132177.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Secretary_Pompeo_Participates_in_Signing_Ceremony_for_the_CSL_Lease_Extension_-_48342132177.jpg/330px-Secretary_Pompeo_Participates_in_Signing_Ceremony_for_the_CSL_Lease_Extension_-_48342132177.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Secretary_Pompeo_Participates_in_Signing_Ceremony_for_the_CSL_Lease_Extension_-_48342132177.jpg/440px-Secretary_Pompeo_Participates_in_Signing_Ceremony_for_the_CSL_Lease_Extension_-_48342132177.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4347" data-file-height="2898"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_Participates_in_Signing_Ceremony_for_the_CSL_Lease_Extension_-_48342132177.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>U.S. Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Mike_Pompeo" title="Mike Pompeo">Mike Pompeo</a> participates in a signing ceremony for the CSL Lease Extension with Salvadoran President <a href="/wiki/Nayib_Bukele" title="Nayib Bukele">Nayib Bukele</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>El Salvador is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> and several of its specialized agencies, including the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Central_American_Parliament" title="Central American Parliament">Central American Parliament</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Central_American_Integration_System" title="Central American Integration System">Central American Integration System</a>. It actively participates in the Central American Security Commission, which seeks to promote regional arms control. El Salvador is a member of the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> and is pursuing regional free trade agreements. An active participant in the <a href="/wiki/Summits_of_the_Americas" title="Summits of the Americas">Summit of the Americas</a> process, El Salvador chairs a working group on market access under the <a href="/wiki/Free_Trade_Area_of_the_Americas" title="Free Trade Area of the Americas">Free Trade Area of the Americas</a> initiative. </p>
      <p>In November, 1950 El Salvador helped the newly empowered <a href="/wiki/14th_Dalai_Lama" title="14th Dalai Lama">14th Dalai Lama</a> by supporting his <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibetan</a> Government cabinet minister's telegram requesting an appeal before the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">General Assembly of the United Nations</a> to stop the Communist <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>'s <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People's Liberation Army">People's Liberation Army</a>'s invasion of Tibet. "Only the tiny country of El Salvador agreed to sponsor Tibet's plea."<sup id="cite_ref-:0_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-79">[79]</a></sup>"At the UN, no one was willing to stand up beside El Salvador. The other nations had overriding self-interests, which made it impossible for them to support San Salvador's attempt to bring the invasion before the General Assembly."<sup id="cite_ref-:0_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-79">[79]</a></sup> With no other countries in support, "the UN unanimously dropped the Tibetan plea from its agenda."<sup id="cite_ref-:0_79-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-79">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>El Salvador has an army, air force, and modest navy. There are around 17,000 personnel in the armed forces in total.<sup id="cite_ref-nationmaster_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nationmaster-80">[80]</a></sup> In 2017, El Salvador signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_El_Salvador" title="Human rights in El Salvador">Human rights in El Salvador</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Amnesty International has drawn attention to several arrests of police officers for unlawful police killings. Other issues to gain Amnesty International's attention include missing children, failure of law enforcement to properly investigate and prosecute crimes against women, and rendering <a href="/wiki/Labor_unions" class="mw-redirect" title="Labor unions">organized labour</a> illegal.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Discrimination against <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_El_Salvador" title="LGBT rights in El Salvador">LGBT people</a> in El Salvador is very widespread.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> According to 2013 survey by the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a>, 62% of Salvadorans believe that <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuality</a> should not be accepted by society.<sup id="cite_ref-pewglobal.org_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pewglobal.org-86">[86]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_El_Salvador" title="Departments of El Salvador">Departments of El Salvador</a>
      </div> 
      <p>El Salvador is <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_El_Salvador" title="Departments of El Salvador">divided into 14 departments</a> (<i>departamentos</i>), which in turn are subdivided into 262 <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_El_Salvador" title="Municipalities of El Salvador">municipalities</a> (<i>municipios</i>). </p>
      <p>Department names and capitals for the 14 Salvadoran Departments: </p> 
      <table class="wikitable center" style="line-height:140%;font-size: 90%;">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_El_Salvador" title="Economy of El Salvador">Economy of El Salvador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:El_Salvador_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/El_Salvador_Export_Treemap.jpg/400px-El_Salvador_Export_Treemap.jpg" decoding="async" width="400" height="313" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/El_Salvador_Export_Treemap.jpg/600px-El_Salvador_Export_Treemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/El_Salvador_Export_Treemap.jpg/800px-El_Salvador_Export_Treemap.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1101" data-file-height="861"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:El_Salvador_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A proportional representation of El Salvador's exports
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>El Salvador's economy has been hampered at times by natural disasters such as earthquakes and hurricanes, by government policies that mandate large economic subsidies, and by official corruption. Subsidies became such a problem that in April 2012, the International Monetary Fund suspended a $750&nbsp;million loan to the central government. President Funes' chief of cabinet, Alex Segovia, acknowledged that the economy was at the "point of collapse".<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Gross domestic product (<a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a>) in <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> in 2008 was estimated at US$25.895&nbsp;billion. The service sector is the largest component of GDP at 64.1%, followed by the industrial sector at 24.7% (2008 est.). Agriculture represents 11.2% of GDP (2010 est.) The GDP grew after 1996 at an annual rate that averaged 3.2% real growth. The government committed to free market initiatives, and the 2007 GDP's real growth rate was 4.7%.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In December 1999, net international reserves equalled US$1.8&nbsp;billion or roughly five months of imports. Having this hard currency buffer to work with, the Salvadoran government undertook a monetary integration plan beginning in January 2001 by which the U.S. dollar became legal tender alongside the <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_col%C3%B3n" title="Salvadoran colón">Salvadoran colón</a>, and all formal accounting was done in U.S. dollars. Thus, the government has formally limited the implementing of open market monetary policies to influence short-term variables in the economy. With the adoption of the U.S. dollar, El Salvador lost control over monetary policy. Any counter-cyclical policy response to the downturn must be through fiscal policy, which is constrained by legislative requirements for a two-thirds majority to approve any international financing. As of September 2007, net <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_reserves" title="Foreign exchange reserves">international reserves</a> stood at $2.42&nbsp;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-tdfiyp_71-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tdfiyp-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>It has long been a challenge in El Salvador to develop new growth sectors for a more diversified economy. In the past, the country produced gold and silver,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> but recent attempts to reopen the mining sector, which were expected to add hundreds of millions of dollars to the local economy, collapsed after President Saca shut down the operations of <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Rim_Mining_Corporation" title="Pacific Rim Mining Corporation">Pacific Rim Mining Corporation</a>. Nevertheless, according to the Central American Institute for Fiscal Studies (Instituto Centroamericano for Estudios Fiscales), the contribution of metallic mining was a minuscule 0.3% of the country's GDP between 2010 and 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Saca's decision although not lacking political motives, had strong support from local residents and grassroots movements in the country. President Funes later rejected a company's application for a further permit based on the risk of cyanide contamination on one of the country's main rivers.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As with other former colonies, El Salvador was considered a mono-export economy (an economy that depended heavily on one type of export) for many years. During colonial times, El Salvador was a thriving exporter of <a href="/wiki/Indigo_dye" title="Indigo dye">indigo</a>, but after the invention of synthetic dyes in the 19th century, the newly created modern state turned to <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a> as the main export. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Fdpt18102006bmcha43c.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Fdpt18102006bmcha43c.jpg/220px-Fdpt18102006bmcha43c.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Fdpt18102006bmcha43c.jpg/330px-Fdpt18102006bmcha43c.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Fdpt18102006bmcha43c.jpg/440px-Fdpt18102006bmcha43c.jpg 2x" data-file-width="595" data-file-height="355"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Fdpt18102006bmcha43c.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/San_Miguel,_El_Salvador" title="San Miguel, El Salvador">San Miguel</a> is an important economic centre of El Salvador and home to the "Carnival of San Miguel", one of the biggest festivals of entertainment and food in Central America.<sup id="cite_ref-Herrera-Sobek2012_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Herrera-Sobek2012-93">[93]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The government has sought to improve the collection of its current revenues, with a focus on indirect taxes. A 10% <a href="/wiki/Value-added_tax" title="Value-added tax">value-added tax</a> (IVA in Spanish), implemented in September 1992, was raised to 13% in July 1995. Inflation has been steady and among the lowest in the region. Since 1997 inflation has averaged 3%, with recent years increasing to nearly 5%. As a result of the free trade agreements, from 2000 to 2006, total exports have grown 19% from $2.94&nbsp;billion to $3.51&nbsp;billion, and total imports have risen 54% from $4.95&nbsp;billion to $7.63&nbsp;billion. This has resulted in a 102% increase in the trade deficit, from $2.01&nbsp;billion to $4.12&nbsp;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:El_Chorreron,_San_Fernando,_El_Salvador.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/El_Chorreron%2C_San_Fernando%2C_El_Salvador.jpg/170px-El_Chorreron%2C_San_Fernando%2C_El_Salvador.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/El_Chorreron%2C_San_Fernando%2C_El_Salvador.jpg/255px-El_Chorreron%2C_San_Fernando%2C_El_Salvador.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/El_Chorreron%2C_San_Fernando%2C_El_Salvador.jpg/340px-El_Chorreron%2C_San_Fernando%2C_El_Salvador.jpg 2x" data-file-width="432" data-file-height="581"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:El_Chorreron,_San_Fernando,_El_Salvador.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>El Chorreron, El Salvador; tourism is the fastest-growing sector of the Salvadoran economy.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>El Salvador has promoted an open trade and investment environment and has embarked on a wave of privatization extending to telecommunications, electricity distribution, banking, and pension funds. In late 2006, the government and the Millennium Challenge Corporation signed a five-year, $461&nbsp;million compact to stimulate economic growth and reduce poverty in the country's northern region, the primary conflict zone during the civil war, through investments in education, public services, enterprise development, and transportation infrastructure. </p>
      <p>In 2006, El Salvador was the first country to ratify the Central America-Dominican Republic Free Trade Agreement (CAFTA) — negotiated by the five countries of Central America and the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> — with the United States. CAFTA requires that the Salvadoran government adopt policies that foster <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">free trade</a>. CAFTA has bolstered exports of processed foods, sugar, and ethanol, and supported investment in the apparel sector, which faced Asian competition with the expiration of the <a href="/wiki/Multi_Fibre_Arrangement" title="Multi Fibre Arrangement">Multi Fibre Arrangement</a> in 2005. In anticipation of the declines in the apparel sector's competitiveness, the previous administration sought to diversify the economy by promoting the country as a regional distribution and logistics hub, and by promoting tourism investment through tax incentives. </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Remittances_from_abroad">Remittances from abroad</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Remittances from abroad">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>El Salvador leads the region in <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittances</a> per capita, with inflows equivalent to nearly all export income; about a third of all households receive these financial inflows. Remittances from Salvadorans living and working in the United States, sent to family members in El Salvador, are a major source of foreign income and offset the substantial trade deficit of $4.12&nbsp;billion. Remittances have increased steadily in the last decade, and reached an all-time high of $3.32&nbsp;billion in 2006 (an increase of 17% over the previous year).<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> approximately 16.2% of GDP. </p>
      <p>Remittances have had positive and negative effects on El Salvador. In 2005, the number of people living in <a href="/wiki/Extreme_poverty" title="Extreme poverty">extreme poverty</a> in El Salvador was 20%,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> according to a United Nations Development Program report. Without remittances, the number of Salvadorans living in extreme poverty would rise to 37%. While Salvadoran education levels have gone up, wage expectations have risen faster than either skills or productivity. For example, some Salvadorans are no longer willing to take jobs that pay them less than what they receive monthly from family members abroad. This has led to an influx of Hondurans and Nicaraguans who are willing to work for the prevailing wage. Also, the local propensity for consumption over investment has increased. </p>
      <p> Money from remittances has increased prices for certain commodities such as real estate. With much higher wages, many Salvadorans abroad can afford higher prices for houses in El Salvador than local Salvadorans, and thus push up the prices that all Salvadorans must pay.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:World_Trade_Center_San_Salvador.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/World_Trade_Center_San_Salvador.jpg/170px-World_Trade_Center_San_Salvador.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/World_Trade_Center_San_Salvador.jpg/255px-World_Trade_Center_San_Salvador.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/World_Trade_Center_San_Salvador.jpg/340px-World_Trade_Center_San_Salvador.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3968" data-file-height="2976"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:World_Trade_Center_San_Salvador.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Torre_Futura" title="Torre Futura">Torre Futura</a> at <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_San_Salvador" title="World Trade Center San Salvador">World Trade Center San Salvador</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Official_corruption_and_foreign_investment">Official corruption and foreign investment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Official corruption and foreign investment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In an analysis of ARENA's electoral defeat in 2009, the U.S. Embassy in San Salvador pointed to official corruption under the Saca administration as a significant reason for public rejection of continued ARENA government. According to a secret diplomatic cable made public by WikiLeaks, "While the Salvadoran public may be inured to self-serving behaviour by politicians, many in ARENA believe that the brazen manner in which Saca and his people are widely perceived to have used their positions for personal enrichment went beyond the pale. ARENA deputy Roberto d'Aubuisson, son of ARENA founder <a href="/wiki/Roberto_d%27Aubuisson" class="mw-redirect" title="Roberto d'Aubuisson">Roberto d'Aubuisson</a>, told [a U.S. diplomat] that Saca 'deliberately ignored' his Public Works Minister's government contract kickbacks scheme, even after the case was revealed in the press. Furthermore, considerable evidence exists, including from U.S. business sources, that the Saca administration pushed laws and selectively enforced regulations with the specific intent to benefit Saca family business interests."<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Subsequent policies under Funes administrations improved El Salvador to foreign investment, and the World Bank in 2014 rated El Salvador 109, a little better than Belize (118) and Nicaragua (119) in the World Bank's annual "<a href="/wiki/Ease_of_doing_business_index" title="Ease of doing business index">Ease of doing business</a>" index.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As per Santander Trade, a Spanish think tank in foreign investment, "Foreign investment into El Salvador has been steadily growing during the last few years. In 2013, the influx of FDI increased. Nevertheless, El Salvador receives less FDI than other countries of Central America. The government has made little progress in terms of improving the business climate. In addition to this, the limited size of its domestic market, weak infrastructures and institutions, as well as the high level of criminality have been real obstacles to investors. However, El Salvador is the second most "business friendly" country in South America in terms of business taxation. It also has a young and skilled labour force and a strategic geographical position. The country's membership in the DR-CAFTA, as well as its reinforced integration to the C4 countries (producers of cotton) should lead to an increase of FDI."<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Foreign companies have lately resorted to arbitration in international trade tribunals in total disagreement with Salvadoran government policies. In 2008, El Salvador sought international arbitration against Italy's Enel Green Power, on behalf of Salvadoran state-owned electric companies for a geothermal project Enel had invested in. Four years later, Enel indicated it would seek arbitration against El Salvador, blaming the government for technical problems that prevent it from completing its investment.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The government came to its defence claiming that Art 109 of the constitution does not allow any government (regardless of the party they belong), to privatize the resources of the national soil (in this case geothermic energy). The dispute came to an end in December 2014 when both parties came to a settlement, from which no details have been released. The small country had yielded to pressure from the Washington based powerful <a href="/wiki/International_Centre_for_Settlement_of_Investment_Disputes" title="International Centre for Settlement of Investment Disputes">ICSID</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> The U.S. Embassy warned in 2009 that the Salvadoran government's populist policies of mandating artificially low electricity prices were damaging private sector profitability, including the interests of American investors in the energy sector.<sup id="cite_ref-ID_No._09SANSALVADOR1184_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ID_No._09SANSALVADOR1184-103">[103]</a></sup> The U.S. Embassy noted the corruption of El Salvador's judicial system and quietly urged American businesses to include "arbitration clauses, preferably with a foreign venue", when doing business in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-ID_No._09SANSALVADOR47_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ID_No._09SANSALVADOR47-104">[104]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A 2008 report by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Conference_on_Trade_and_Development" title="United Nations Conference on Trade and Development">United Nations Conference on Trade and Development</a> <sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> indicates that one third of the generation of electricity in El Salvador was publicly owned while two thirds was in American hands and other foreign ownership. It is only natural for a small, under-developed country like El Salvador to subsidize some of the resources for the vast majority of its poor population. In terms of how people perceived the levels of public corruption in 2014, El Salvador ranks 80 out of 175 countries as per the Corruption Perception Index.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> El Salvador's rating compares relatively well with Panama (94 of 175) and Costa Rica (47 of 175). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_El_Salvador" title="Tourism in El Salvador">Tourism in El Salvador</a>
      </div> 
      <p>It was estimated that 1,394,000 international tourists visited El Salvador in 2014.Tourism contributed US$2970.1&nbsp;million to El Salvador's GDP in 2019. This represented 11% of total GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-wttc.org_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wttc.org-107">[107]</a></sup> Tourism directly supported 80,500 jobs in 2013. This represented 3.1% of total employment in El Salvador. In 2019, tourism indirectly supported 317,200 jobs, representing 11.6% of total employment in El Salvador.<sup id="cite_ref-wttc.org_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wttc.org-107">[107]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Surfing_in_El_Salvador_by_L._E._MacDonald.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Surfing_in_El_Salvador_by_L._E._MacDonald.png/220px-Surfing_in_El_Salvador_by_L._E._MacDonald.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="115" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Surfing_in_El_Salvador_by_L._E._MacDonald.png/330px-Surfing_in_El_Salvador_by_L._E._MacDonald.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Surfing_in_El_Salvador_by_L._E._MacDonald.png/440px-Surfing_in_El_Salvador_by_L._E._MacDonald.png 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="534"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Surfing_in_El_Salvador_by_L._E._MacDonald.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>El Salvador has surf tourism due to large waves from the Pacific Ocean.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Most North American and European tourists seek out El Salvador's beaches and nightlife. El Salvador's tourism landscape is slightly different from those of other Central American countries. Because of its geographic size and urbanization there are not many nature-themed tourist destinations such as ecotours or archaeological sites open to the public. According to the El Salvadoran newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/El_Diario_De_Hoy" class="mw-redirect" title="El Diario De Hoy">El Diario De Hoy</a></i>, the top 10 attractions are: the coastal beaches, <a href="/wiki/La_Libertad,_La_Libertad" title="La Libertad, La Libertad">La Libertad</a>, Ruta Las Flores, <a href="/wiki/Suchitoto" title="Suchitoto">Suchitoto</a>, Playa Las Flores in <a href="/wiki/San_Miguel,_El_Salvador" title="San Miguel, El Salvador">San Miguel</a>, La Palma, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Volcano" title="Santa Ana Volcano">Santa Ana</a> (location of the country's highest volcano), <a href="/wiki/Nahuizalco" title="Nahuizalco">Nahuizalco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apaneca" title="Apaneca">Apaneca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juayua" class="mw-redirect" title="Juayua">Juayua</a>, and <a href="/wiki/San_Ignacio,_Chalatenango" title="San Ignacio, Chalatenango">San Ignacio</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Surfing is a natural tourism sector that has gained popularity in recent years as Salvadoran beaches have become increasingly popular. Surfers visit many beaches on the coast of La Libertad and the east end of El Salvador. The use of the U.S. dollar as Salvadoran currency and direct flights of 4 to 6 hours from most cities in the United States are factors that attract American tourists. Urbanization and <a href="/wiki/Americanization" title="Americanization">Americanization</a> of Salvadoran culture has led to the abundance of American-style malls, stores, and restaurants in the three main urban areas, especially greater San Salvador. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The level of access <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_El_Salvador" title="Water supply and sanitation in El Salvador">to water supply and sanitation</a> has been increased significantly. A 2015 conducted study by the University of North Carolina called El Salvador the country that has achieved the greatest progress in the world in terms of increased access to water supply and sanitation and the reduction of inequity in access between urban and rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> However, water resources are seriously polluted and a large part of the wastewater discharged into the environment without any treatment. Institutionally a single public institution is both de facto in charge of setting sector policy and of being the main service provider. Attempts at reforming and modernizing the sector through new laws have not borne fruit over the past 20 years. </p>
      <p>The airport serving international flights in El Salvador is <a href="/wiki/Monse%C3%B1or_%C3%93scar_Arnulfo_Romero_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Monseñor Óscar Arnulfo Romero International Airport">Monseñor Óscar Arnulfo Romero International Airport</a>. This airport is located about 40&nbsp;km (25&nbsp;mi) southeast of San Salvador.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_El_Salvador" title="Demographics of El Salvador">Demographics of El Salvador</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population <sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-5">[5]</a></sup> </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <th style="background:#cfb;">Year </th>

      <p>El Salvador's population was 6,420,746 in 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-5">[5]</a></sup> compared to 2,200,000 in 1950. In 2010 the percentage of the population below the age of 15 was 32.1%, 61% were between 15 and 65 years of age, while 6.9% were 65 years or older.<sup id="cite_ref-WPP_2012_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WPP_2012-111">[111]</a></sup> The capital city of San Salvador has a population of about 2.1&nbsp;million people. An estimated 42% of El Salvador's population live in rural areas. <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">Urbanization</a> has expanded at a phenomenal rate in El Salvador since the 1960s, with millions moving to the cities and creating associated problems for urban planning and services. </p>
      <p>There are up to 100,000 Nicaraguans living in El Salvador.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">

       </div> 
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Potada.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Potada.JPG/170px-Potada.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Potada.JPG/255px-Potada.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/ff/Potada.JPG 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Potada.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Salvadoran model <a href="/wiki/Irma_Dimas" title="Irma Dimas">Irma Dimas</a> was crowned Miss El Salvador in 2005. She made headlines recently for her entry into Salvadoran politics.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>El Salvador's population is composed of mixed races as well as people of indigenous, European, or Afro-descendant ancestry among smaller diasporas of Middle and Far Eastern groups. Eighty-six per cent of Salvadorans identify with mestizo ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-113">[113]</a></sup> 12.7% of Salvadorans report as <a href="/wiki/White_Latin_American#El_Salvador" class="mw-redirect" title="White Latin American">White</a>, mostly of ethnically <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spanish people</a>, while there are also Salvadorans of <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swiss_people" title="Swiss people">Swiss</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irish</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italian</a> descent. Most Central European immigrants in El Salvador arrived during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> as refugees from the Czech Republic, Germany, Hungary, Poland, and Switzerland. There are also small communities of Jews, Palestinian Christians, and Arab Muslims (in particular <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Salvadoran" title="Palestinian Salvadoran">Palestinians</a>). </p>
      <p>0.23% of the population report as fully indigenous. The ethnic groups are Kakawira which represents 0.07% of the total country's population, <a href="/wiki/Pipil_people" title="Pipil people">Nawat</a> (0.06%), <a href="/wiki/Lenca_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Lenca people">Lenca</a> (0.04%) and other minor groups (0.06%). Very few Amerindians have retained their customs and traditions, having over time assimilated into the dominant mestizo culture.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> There is a small <a href="/wiki/Afro-Salvadorans" title="Afro-Salvadorans">Afro-Salvadoran</a> group that is 0.13% of the total population, with Blacks, among other races, having been prevented from immigrating via government policies in the early 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-B_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-B-116">[116]</a></sup> The descendants of enslaved Africans, however, had already integrated into the Salvadoran population and culture well before, during the colonial and post-colonial period.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Among the immigrant groups in El Salvador, Palestinian Christians stand out.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Though few in number, their descendants have attained great economic and political power in the country, as evidenced by the election of President <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Saca" title="Antonio Saca">Antonio Saca</a>, whose opponent in the 2004 election, <a href="/wiki/Schafik_Handal" title="Schafik Handal">Schafik Handal</a>, was also of Palestinian descent, and the flourishing commercial, industrial, and construction firms owned by this ethnic group. </p>
      <p>As of 2004<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were approximately 3.2&nbsp;million Salvadorans living outside El Salvador, with the United States traditionally being the destination of choice for Salvadoran economic migrants. By 2012, there were about 2.0&nbsp;million Salvadoran immigrants and <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_Americans" title="Salvadoran Americans">Americans of Salvadoran descent</a> in the U.S.,<sup id="cite_ref-2012AmericanCommunitySurvey_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012AmericanCommunitySurvey-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> making them the sixth largest immigrant group in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> The second destination of Salvadorans living outside is Guatemala, with more than 111,000 persons, mainly in <a href="/wiki/Guatemala_City" title="Guatemala City">Guatemala City</a>. Salvadorans also live in other nearby countries such as Belize, Honduras and Nicaragua.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Other countries with notable Salvadoran communities include Canada, Mexico, the United Kingdom (including the Cayman Islands), Sweden, Brazil, Italy, Colombia, and Australia. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Beatificacion_Monse%C3%B1or_Romero_(18012123351).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Beatificacion_Monse%C3%B1or_Romero_%2818012123351%29.jpg/220px-Beatificacion_Monse%C3%B1or_Romero_%2818012123351%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Beatificacion_Monse%C3%B1or_Romero_%2818012123351%29.jpg/330px-Beatificacion_Monse%C3%B1or_Romero_%2818012123351%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Beatificacion_Monse%C3%B1or_Romero_%2818012123351%29.jpg/440px-Beatificacion_Monse%C3%B1or_Romero_%2818012123351%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3720" data-file-height="2928"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Beatificacion_Monse%C3%B1or_Romero_(18012123351).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Salvadoran children hold a picture of <a href="/wiki/%C3%93scar_Romero" title="Óscar Romero">Óscar Romero</a> during his beatification
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Castillian, also known as Spanish, is the official language and is spoken by virtually all inhabitants, although some indigenous people speak also their native tongues, such as <a href="/wiki/Pipil_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Pipil language">Nawat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poqomam_language" title="Poqomam language">Poqomam</a>. <a href="/wiki/Q%27eqchi%27_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Q'eqchi' language">Q'eqchi'</a> is spoken by immigrants of <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemalan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belizean</a> indigenous people living in El Salvador. </p>
      <p>Like other regions of Central and South America, Salvadoran use <a href="/wiki/Voseo" title="Voseo">voseo</a>. This refers to the use of "vos" as the second person pronoun, instead of "tú".The local Spanish <a href="/wiki/Vernacular" title="Vernacular">vernacular</a> is called <i><a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_Spanish" title="Salvadoran Spanish">caliche</a>,</i> which is considered informal. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities">Largest cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Largest cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_El_Salvador" title="List of cities in El Salvador">List of cities in El Salvador</a>
      </div>

       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th colspan="10" class="navbox-title">

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_El_Salvador" title="Religion in El Salvador">Religion in El Salvador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">

       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>The majority of the population in El Salvador is <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a>. <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholics</a> (47%) and <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestants</a> (33%) are the two major religious groups in the country, with the Catholic Church the largest denomination.<sup id="cite_ref-IRFR2012_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR2012-124">[124]</a></sup> Those not affiliated with any religious group amount to 17% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-IRFR2012_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR2012-124">[124]</a></sup> The remainder of the population (3%) is made up of <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hare_Krishnas" class="mw-redirect" title="Hare Krishnas">Hare Krishnas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhists" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhists">Buddhists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latter-day_Saints" class="mw-redirect" title="Latter-day Saints">Latter-day Saints</a>, and those adhering to indigenous religious beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-IRFR2012_124-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR2012-124">[124]</a></sup> The number of evangelicals in the country is growing rapidly.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/%C3%93scar_Romero" title="Óscar Romero">Óscar Romero</a>, the first Salvadoran saint, was canonized by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a> on 14 October 2018. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_El_Salvador" title="Education in El Salvador">Education in El Salvador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Asociaci%C3%B3n_Salvadore%C3%B1a_de_Astronom%C3%ADa_Observatorio_%22Dr._Prudencio_Llach%22.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Asociaci%C3%B3n_Salvadore%C3%B1a_de_Astronom%C3%ADa_Observatorio_%22Dr._Prudencio_Llach%22.jpg/220px-Asociaci%C3%B3n_Salvadore%C3%B1a_de_Astronom%C3%ADa_Observatorio_%22Dr._Prudencio_Llach%22.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Asociaci%C3%B3n_Salvadore%C3%B1a_de_Astronom%C3%ADa_Observatorio_%22Dr._Prudencio_Llach%22.jpg/330px-Asociaci%C3%B3n_Salvadore%C3%B1a_de_Astronom%C3%ADa_Observatorio_%22Dr._Prudencio_Llach%22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Asociaci%C3%B3n_Salvadore%C3%B1a_de_Astronom%C3%ADa_Observatorio_%22Dr._Prudencio_Llach%22.jpg/440px-Asociaci%C3%B3n_Salvadore%C3%B1a_de_Astronom%C3%ADa_Observatorio_%22Dr._Prudencio_Llach%22.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6016" data-file-height="4000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Asociaci%C3%B3n_Salvadore%C3%B1a_de_Astronom%C3%ADa_Observatorio_%22Dr._Prudencio_Llach%22.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Dr. Prudencio Llach Observatory
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The public education system in El Salvador is severely lacking in resources. Class sizes in public schools can be as large as 50 children per classroom. Salvadorans who can afford the cost often choose to send their children to private schools, which are regarded as being better-quality than public schools. Most private schools follow American, European or other advanced systems. Lower-income families are forced to rely on public education.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Education in El Salvador is free through high school. After nine years of basic education (elementary–middle school), students have the option of a two-year high school or a three-year high school. A two-year high school prepares the student for transfer to a university. A three-year high school allows the student to graduate and enter the workforce in a vocational career, or to transfer to a university to further their education in their chosen field.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_El_Salvador" title="List of universities in El Salvador">Universities in El Salvador</a> include a central public institution, the <a href="/wiki/Universidad_de_El_Salvador" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidad de El Salvador">Universidad de El Salvador</a>, and many other specialized private universities. </p>
