      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:PNC-02N_MD_Helicopters_MD520N_El_Salvador_Policia_(7486576752).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/PNC-02N_MD_Helicopters_MD520N_El_Salvador_Policia_%287486576752%29.jpg/220px-PNC-02N_MD_Helicopters_MD520N_El_Salvador_Policia_%287486576752%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/PNC-02N_MD_Helicopters_MD520N_El_Salvador_Policia_%287486576752%29.jpg/330px-PNC-02N_MD_Helicopters_MD520N_El_Salvador_Policia_%287486576752%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/PNC-02N_MD_Helicopters_MD520N_El_Salvador_Policia_%287486576752%29.jpg/440px-PNC-02N_MD_Helicopters_MD520N_El_Salvador_Policia_%287486576752%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:PNC-02N_MD_Helicopters_MD520N_El_Salvador_Policia_(7486576752).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/National_Civil_Police_of_El_Salvador" title="National Civil Police of El Salvador">National Civil Police of El Salvador</a> helicopter
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since the early twenty-first century, El Salvador has experienced high crime rates, including gang-related crimes and <a href="/wiki/Juvenile_delinquency" title="Juvenile delinquency">juvenile delinquency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> El Salvador had the highest murder rate in the world in 2012 but experienced a sharp decline in 2019 with a new centrist government in power.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> It is also considered an epicentre of a gang crisis, along with Guatemala and Honduras.<sup id="cite_ref-FAS_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAS-131">[131]</a></sup> In response to this, the government has set up countless programs to try to guide the youth away from gang membership; so far its efforts have not produced any quick results. One of the government programs was a gang reform called "<a href="/wiki/La_Mano_Dura" title="La Mano Dura">Super Mano Dura</a>" (Super Firm Hand). Super Mano Dura had little success and was highly criticized by the United Nations. It experienced temporary success in 2004 but there was a rise in crime after 2005. In 2004, there were 41 intentional homicides per 100,000 citizens, with 60% of the homicides committed being gang-related.<sup id="cite_ref-FAS_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAS-131">[131]</a></sup> In 2012, the homicide rate had increased to 66 per 100,000 inhabitants, more than triple the rate in Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-NYRB_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYRB-132">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> There are an estimated 25,000 gang members at large in El Salvador with another 9,000 in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-NYRB_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYRB-132">[132]</a></sup> The most well-known gangs, called "<a href="/wiki/Mara_(gang)" title="Mara (gang)">maras</a>" in colloquial Spanish, are <a href="/wiki/MS-13" title="MS-13">Mara Salvatrucha</a> and their rivals <a href="/wiki/18th_Street_gang" title="18th Street gang">Barrio 18</a>. Maras are hunted by <a href="/wiki/Death_squad" title="Death squad">death squads</a> including <a href="/wiki/Sombra_Negra" title="Sombra Negra">Sombra Negra</a>. New rivals also include the rising mara, The Rebels 13.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of March&nbsp;2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, El Salvador has seen a 40% drop in crime due to what the Salvadoran government called a gang truce; however, extortion affecting small businesses are not taken into account. In early 2012, there were an average of 16 killings per day; in late March of that year that number dropped to fewer than 5 per day. On 14 April 2012 for the first time in over 3 years there were no killings in El Salvador.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> Overall, there were 411 killings in January 2012, and in March the number was 188, more than a 40% reduction,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> while crime in neighbouring Honduras had risen to an all-time high.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> In 2014, crime rose 56% in El Salvador, with the government attributing the rise to a break in the truce between the two major gangs in El Salvador, which began having turf wars.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Presently, the <i><i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">Alto al Crimen</i></i> or <a href="/wiki/Crime_Stoppers" title="Crime Stoppers">Crime Stoppers</a> program is in operation and provides financial rewards for information leading to the capture of gang leadership. The reward often ranges between US$100 and $500 per call.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_El_Salvador" title="Culture of El Salvador">Culture of El Salvador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:SalvadorDelMundo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/SalvadorDelMundo.jpg/220px-SalvadorDelMundo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="344" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/SalvadorDelMundo.jpg/330px-SalvadorDelMundo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/SalvadorDelMundo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="409" data-file-height="640"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:SalvadorDelMundo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The iconic statue of Christ on the globe sphere of planet earth is part of the <a href="/wiki/Monumento_al_Divino_Salvador_del_Mundo" title="Monumento al Divino Salvador del Mundo">Monumento al Divino Salvador del Mundo</a> ('Monument to the Divine Saviour of the World') on Plaza El Salvador del Mundo ('The Saviour of the World Plaza'), a landmark located in the country's capital, San Salvador.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Pulling from indigenous, colonial Spanish and African influences, a composite population was formed as a result of intermarrying between the natives, European settlers, and enslaved Africans. The Catholic Church plays an important role in the Salvadoran culture. Archbishop <a href="/wiki/%C3%93scar_Romero" title="Óscar Romero">Óscar Romero</a> is a national hero for his role in resisting human rights violations that were occurring in the lead-up to the Salvadoran Civil War.<sup id="cite_ref-Eaton_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eaton-141">[141]</a></sup> Significant foreign personalities in El Salvador were the Jesuit priests and professors <a href="/wiki/Ignacio_Ellacur%C3%ADa" title="Ignacio Ellacuría">Ignacio Ellacuría</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ignacio_Mart%C3%ADn-Bar%C3%B3" title="Ignacio Martín-Baró">Ignacio Martín-Baró</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Segundo_Montes" title="Segundo Montes">Segundo Montes</a>, who were murdered in 1989 by the Salvadoran Army during the height of the civil war. </p>
      <p>Painting, ceramics and textiles are the principal manual artistic mediums. Writers <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Gavidia" title="Francisco Gavidia">Francisco Gavidia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salarru%C3%A9" title="Salarrué">Salarrué</a> (Salvador Salazar Arrué), <a href="/wiki/Claudia_Lars" title="Claudia Lars">Claudia Lars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Espino" title="Alfredo Espino">Alfredo Espino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Geoffroy_Rivas" title="Pedro Geoffroy Rivas">Pedro Geoffroy Rivas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manlio_Argueta" title="Manlio Argueta">Manlio Argueta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Roberto_Cea" title="José Roberto Cea">José Roberto Cea</a>, and poet <a href="/wiki/Roque_Dalton" title="Roque Dalton">Roque Dalton</a> are important writers from El Salvador. Notable 20th-century personages include the late filmmaker Baltasar Polio, female film director <a href="/wiki/Patricia_Chica" title="Patricia Chica">Patricia Chica</a>, artist <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Llort" title="Fernando Llort">Fernando Llort</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Caricaturist" class="mw-redirect" title="Caricaturist">caricaturist</a> <a href="/wiki/To%C3%B1o_Salazar" title="Toño Salazar">Toño Salazar</a>. </p>
      <p>Among the more renowned representatives of the graphic arts are the painters <a href="/wiki/Augusto_Crespin" title="Augusto Crespin">Augusto Crespin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noe_Canjura" title="Noe Canjura">Noe Canjura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Ca%C3%B1as" title="Carlos Cañas">Carlos Cañas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Gil" title="Giovanni Gil">Giovanni Gil</a>, Julia Díaz, Mauricio Mejia, Maria Elena Palomo de Mejia, <a href="/wiki/Camilo_Minero" title="Camilo Minero">Camilo Minero</a>, Ricardo Carbonell, Roberto Huezo, Miguel Angel Cerna, (the painter and writer better known as MACLo), Esael Araujo, and many others. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_holidays">Public holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Public holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_cuisine" title="Salvadoran cuisine">Salvadoran cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Plain_pupusas_revueltas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Plain_pupusas_revueltas.jpg/220px-Plain_pupusas_revueltas.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Plain_pupusas_revueltas.jpg/330px-Plain_pupusas_revueltas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Plain_pupusas_revueltas.jpg/440px-Plain_pupusas_revueltas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Plain_pupusas_revueltas.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i>Pupusas</i>, the national and most famous dish of El Salvador.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sopa_de_pata.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Sopa_de_pata.jpg/220px-Sopa_de_pata.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Sopa_de_pata.jpg/330px-Sopa_de_pata.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Sopa_de_pata.jpg/440px-Sopa_de_pata.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2459" data-file-height="1800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sopa_de_pata.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i><a href="/wiki/Sopa_de_pata" title="Sopa de pata">Sopa de pata</a></i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>One of El Salvador's notable dishes is the <i><a href="/wiki/Pupusa" title="Pupusa">pupusa</a></i>. <i>Pupusas</i> are handmade corn tortillas (made of <i><a href="/wiki/Masa" title="Masa">masa de maíz</a></i> or <i>masa de arroz</i>, a maize or rice flour dough used in <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_cuisine" title="Latin American cuisine">Latin American cuisine</a>) stuffed with one or more of the following: cheese (usually a soft Salvadoran cheese such as <i><a href="/wiki/Quesillo" title="Quesillo">quesillo</a></i>, similar to mozzarella), <i><a href="/wiki/Chicharr%C3%B3n" title="Chicharrón">chicharrón</a></i>, or <a href="/wiki/Refried_beans" title="Refried beans">refried beans</a>. Sometimes the filling is <i>queso con loroco</i> (cheese combined with <i><a href="/wiki/Loroco" class="mw-redirect" title="Loroco">loroco</a></i>, a vine flower bud native to Central America).<sup id="cite_ref-Elsalvador.com_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elsalvador.com-143">[143]</a></sup> <i>Pupusas revueltas</i> are <i>pupusas</i> filled with beans, cheese and pork. There are also vegetarian options. Some adventurous restaurants even offer <i>pupusas</i> stuffed with shrimp or spinach. The name <i>pupusa</i> comes from the Pipil-Nahuatl word, <i>pupushahua</i>. The origins of the <i>pupusa</i> are debated, although its presence in El Salvador is known to predate the arrival of the Spaniards.<sup id="cite_ref-Elsalvador.com_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elsalvador.com-143">[143]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Two other typical Salvadoran dishes are <i>yuca frita</i> and <i>panes con pollo</i>. <i>Yuca frita</i> is deep fried <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a> root served with <a href="/wiki/Curtido" title="Curtido">curtido</a> (a pickled cabbage, onion and carrot topping) and pork rinds with <i>pescaditas</i> (fried baby sardines). Yuca is sometimes served boiled instead of fried. <i>Pan con pollo/pavo</i> (bread with chicken/turkey) are warm turkey or chicken-filled submarine sandwiches. The bird is marinated and then roasted with spices and hand-pulled. This sandwich is traditionally served with tomato and watercress along with cucumber, onion, lettuce, mayonnaise, and mustard. </p>
      <p>One of El Salvador's typical breakfasts is fried plantain, usually served with cream. It is common in Salvadoran restaurants and homes, including those of immigrants to the United States. <a href="/wiki/Alguashte" title="Alguashte">Alguashte</a>, a condiment made from dried, ground <a href="/wiki/Pepitas" class="mw-redirect" title="Pepitas">pepitas</a>, is commonly incorporated into savoury and sweet Salvadoran dishes. "<i>Maria Luisa</i>" is a dessert commonly found in El Salvador. It is a layered cake that is soaked in orange marmalade and sprinkled with powdered sugar. One of the most popular desserts is the cake <i>Pastel de tres leches</i> (Cake of three milks), consisting of three types of milk: evaporated milk, condensed milk, and cream. </p>
      <p>A popular drink that Salvadorans enjoy is <i><a href="/wiki/Horchata" title="Horchata">horchata</a></i>. <i>Horchata</i> is most commonly made of the <a href="/wiki/Morro_seed" class="mw-redirect" title="Morro seed">morro seed</a> ground into a powder and added to milk or water, and sugar. <i>Horchata</i> is drank year-round, and can be drank at any time of day. It mostly is accompanied by a plate of <i>pupusas</i> or fried yuca. <i>Horchata</i> from El Salvador has a very distinct taste and is not to be confused with Mexican <i>horchata</i>, which is rice-based. Coffee is also a common morning beverage.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> Other popular drinks in El Salvador include e<i>nsalada</i>, a drink made of chopped fruit swimming in fruit juice, and <i>Kolachampan</i>, a sugar cane-flavoured carbonated beverage. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_El_Salvador" title="Music of El Salvador">Music of El Salvador</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Traditional Salvadoran music is a mixture of indigenous, Spanish, and African influences. It includes religious songs (mostly used to celebrate Christmas and other holidays, especially feast days of the saints). Other musical repertoire consists of danza, pasillo, marcha and cancione which are composed of parading bands, street performances, or onstage dances, either in groups or paired. Satirical and rural lyrical themes are common. Traditional instruments used are the <i><a href="/wiki/Marimba" title="Marimba">marimba</a></i>, <i>tepehuaste</i>, flutes, drums, <a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCiro" title="Güiro">scrapers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gourd" title="Gourd">gourds</a>, as well as guitars among others. El Salvador's well known folk dance is known as <i><a href="/wiki/Xuc" title="Xuc">Xuc</a></i> which originated in <a href="/wiki/Cojutepeque" title="Cojutepeque">Cojutepeque</a>, Cuscatlan. Caribbean, Colombian, and Mexican music has become customary listening radio and party in the country, especially boleros, cumbia, merengue, Latin pop, salsa, bachata, and reggaeton. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_El_Salvador" class="mw-redirect" title="Sport in El Salvador">Sport in El Salvador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Monumental_Estadio_Cuscatlan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Monumental_Estadio_Cuscatlan.jpg/220px-Monumental_Estadio_Cuscatlan.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Monumental_Estadio_Cuscatlan.jpg/330px-Monumental_Estadio_Cuscatlan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Monumental_Estadio_Cuscatlan.jpg/440px-Monumental_Estadio_Cuscatlan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3968" data-file-height="2976"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Monumental_Estadio_Cuscatlan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Estadio_Cuscatl%C3%A1n" title="Estadio Cuscatlán">Estadio Cuscatlán</a> in San Salvador is the largest stadium in Central America
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in El Salvador. The <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador_national_football_team" title="El Salvador national football team">El Salvador national football team</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/1970_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1970 FIFA World Cup">1970</a> and <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982</a>. Their qualification for the 1970 tournament was marred by the <a href="/wiki/Football_War" title="Football War">Football War</a>, a war against <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a>, whose team El Salvador's had defeated. The national football team play at the <a href="/wiki/Estadio_Cuscatl%C3%A1n" title="Estadio Cuscatlán">Estadio Cuscatlán</a> in San Salvador. It opened in 1976 and seats 53,400, making it the largest stadium in Central America and the Caribbean.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Further reading">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <ul>
       <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://2009-2017.state.gov/r/pa/ei/bgn/2033.htm">"Background Notes"</a>, <i>Background Notes: El Salvador</i>, January 2008. Retrieved 6 March 2008.</li> 
       <li>Bonner, Raymond. <i>Weakness and Deceit: U.S. Policy and El Salvador</i>. New York: Times Books, 1984.</li> 
       <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.cia.gov/the-world-factbook/countries/el-salvador/"><i>CIA World Factbook</i></a>, "El Salvador", 28 February 2008. Retrieved 6 March 2008.</li> 
       <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20100510070619/http://travel.state.gov/travel/cis_pa_tw/cis/cis_1109.html">"Country Specific Information"</a>, <i>U.S. State Department</i>, 3 October 2007. Retrieved 6 March 2008.</li> 
       <li>Danner, Mark. <i>The Massacre at El Mozote: A Parable of the Cold War</i>. New York: Vintage Books, 1994.</li> 
       <li>Foley, Erin. 'Cultures of the world, El Salvador. 1995</li> 
       <li>Montgomery, Tommie Sue. <i>Revolution in El Salvador: From Civil Strife to Civil Peace</i>. Boulder, Colorado: Westview Press, 1995.</li> 
       <li>
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFRosa1998" class="citation thesis cs1">Rosa, Audrey Celeste (1998). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://scholars.wlu.ca/etd/661/"><i>The courage to change: Salvadoran stories of personal and social transformation (El Salvador)</i></a> (M.A. thesis). Wilfrid Laurier University.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Adissertation&amp;rft.title=The+courage+to+change%3A+Salvadoran+stories+of+personal+and+social+transformation+%28El+Salvador%29&amp;rft.degree=M.A.&amp;rft.inst=Wilfrid+Laurier+University&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.aulast=Rosa&amp;rft.aufirst=Audrey+Celeste&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fscholars.wlu.ca%2Fetd%2F661%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEl+Salvador" class="Z3988"></span></li> 
       <li>Stadler, Sidney. <i>It Started with an Oyster: The Memoirs of Sidney M. Stadler, CBE</i>. Penna Press 1975. Autobiography of a British businessman and diplomat in El Salvador, with much on Salvadoran society and politics from the 1920s to 1950s.</li> 
       <li>Vilas, Carlos. <i>Between Earthquakes and Volcanoes: Market, State, and the Revolution America</i>. New York: Monthly Review Press. 1995.</li>
      </ul>
